Title: DLC Data Cleaning and Triangulation
ID: 69c03a2e-9ad8-8386-b079-a9f8528d6723

User: In a simulation setting, I have a Deep Lab Cut tracking result of body parts of two mice for three synchronously taken videos. The extraction results are not bad concerning the body part positions. But relatively often the identities of the two mice are switching. Furthermore, not seldom a body part is assigned to the wrong mouse: While most of the parts are correctly assigned to the two mice, one part may be assigned to the wrong one. 

The DLC data is from three cameras observing a cage from top, front and side. Therefore, finally I want to use the data to compute 3D body part positions from the three videos. But considering the confusion in the data, first I want to - or rather have to - clean the DLC data. For that purpose I processed the data with a segmentation algorithm providing mouse 0 and mouse 1 segments for  the video frames. That semantic segmentation is largely clean. Looking into the neighborhood of each DLC point in the segmentation result would allow to find whether a point belongs to mouse 0 or mouse 1 - at least to some degree.

Algorithmically, in a circle with radius r or a square window of a certain width, height, pixels can be counted with Gaussian weighting (--sigma parameter in pixels; there are rules of thumb in image processing telling how large a window should be for a certain value sigma) resulting in a vector giving weight values for background, mouse 0 and mouse 1).

But in order to use the power of the three perspectives (that is not considered by DLC) I want to triangulate each body part in 3D object space. That's supported by the fact that I have camera exterior and interior orientation parameters in a cameras.json file. That triangulation I want to do very systematically in all possible combinations.

There are ten different body parts of the two mice tracked. If the mouse-assignment is kept undecided but the part id is known for every part id (e.g. nose tip), there are two parts in the three video frames "top", "front" and "side". Potential occlusion certainly occur. So for a part "nose tip" there are 2³=8 possible combinations for 3-ray triangulation (minus combinations involving an occlusion). 

If a combination is from three rays intersecting in 3D space with sufficient accuracy, we have a valid triplet of rays. If the intersection is bad (no convergence in a single-3D-point bundle adjustment), the rays and the image points do not belong together. 

In a secondary attempt (for all points not yet assigned to a triplet) two-ray intersections can be tested in two-ray bundles.

Once no further groups (ray triplets, ray pairs, single rays(i.e. no bundle)) can be found, the assignment to the two mice can be computed. The decision to which mouse a triplet, pair or point belongs depends on the weight vector from the segmentation analysis: If the weight value for assignment to mouse 0, mouse 1 are larger than 0 (not very large but only larger than zero, as the body part may be a tail tip or a nose tip occluding the other mouse), this is a positive vote in favor of mouse 0 / mouse 1. The votes of all three (two for pairs or only one vote for single rays) are summed. In this way each part can cast a vote for both mice, one mouse or no mouse. The mouse that has the majority of votes wins the triplet.

While it may sound like an overkill, I want to implement all single 3D point (three ray or two ray) as a Ceres bundle adjustment. The approximate solutions for initialization can be computed from any two ray spatial intersection with the approximate solutions in the middle of the place where the two rays pass each other (i.e. on the line giving the closest connection between both rays being itself orthogonal to both rays).

Every adjusted 3D point is to be reprojected to the image in order to calculate the delta_x and delta_y residuals from the observed image point. Depending on the  variance-covariance matrix of the residuals computed over all valid triangulations we can decide which ray intersections are valid or not. So on first program run we may need to give a max-delta value for the residual (difference between observed and reprojected). Later on - in second and further runs - that value can be adapted to the variance-covariance matrix.

Assistant: Here’s how I’d pressure-test (and tighten) the algorithmic design before we touch code.

## 1) Reframe the core problem: multi-view data association with 2 identities
Per frame *and* per bodypart you effectively have up to **6 candidate 2D observations** (3 cams × 2 DLC “individuals”), with missingness/occlusions. The hard part is not triangulation itself; it’s **choosing which 2D observations belong to the same physical 3D point**, while enforcing **(a) disjointness** (each 2D obs used at most once) and **(b) exactly up to two 3D points** (two mice) per bodypart per frame.

Your “enumerate all 2³ triplets + fallback to pairs + singles” is fine as a generator of hypotheses, but you’ll want an explicit **selection/optimization step** so you don’t end up with locally-good but globally-inconsistent bundle choices.

## 2) Make triangulation a *hypothesis test* with cheap pruning before Ceres
Doing every hypothesis as a Ceres BA is defensible, but you should prune aggressively first; otherwise the number of BA solves can explode over long sequences.

A good pipeline per frame, per bodypart:

### 2.1 Build observations
For each camera \(c\), and DLC individual \(d\in\{0,1\}\), create an observation if:
- (x,y) finite,
- likelihood \( \ge l_{\min}\),
- segmentation yields weights/probabilities \(p(\text{mouse0}), p(\text{mouse1}), p(\text{bg})\).

### 2.2 Cheap geometric gates (no Ceres yet)
For each candidate triplet/pair:
1) **Ray-angle gate:** reject if smallest pairwise ray angle < θ_min (your idea already).  
2) **Closest-approach distance gate (pairs):** compute the minimum distance between rays; reject if > d_max.  
3) **Bounding box gate:** reject if the implied 3D point is outside the cage volume (you have cage dims in `cameras.json`). fileciteturn0file8  
4) **Fast reprojection gate:** from the closed-form pair midpoint (your proposed initialization), project back and reject if any reprojection error > e_init.

Only if a hypothesis survives these, run the Ceres “single-point BA” to refine and score it.

This way Ceres is used where it matters: scoring close calls and improving final geometry.

## 3) Don’t just “accept/reject” hypotheses — score them, then select disjoint bundles
Even with your “each bodypart can only contribute to one triangulation” constraint, you need a selection rule.

### 3.1 Score a hypothesis = geometric consistency × segmentation support × DLC quality
A practical scoring function for a hypothesis \(H\) (triplet or pair) is:

- **Geometric term**: use final BA residuals as a chi-square-like value  
  \[
  \chi^2(H)=\sum_i \frac{r_{u,i}^2+r_{v,i}^2}{\sigma_{pix,i}^2}
  \]
  (or RMS px if you prefer).
- **Segmentation term**: aggregate log-odds over participating observations for each mouse ID:
  \[
  S_k(H)=\sum_{o\in H}\log\left(\epsilon + p_k(o)\right)
  \]
- **DLC term**: incorporate likelihood similarly (or through \(\sigma_{pix}\) mapping).

Then define:
\[
\text{score}(H,k) = -\tfrac12\chi^2(H) + \alpha S_k(H)
\]
where \(k\in\{0,1\}\) is the mouse identity you’re trying to assign to that 3D point.

### 3.2 Select up to two hypotheses with disjoint observations
For each bodypart/frame you’ll have a small set of candidate triplets and pairs. You can brute-force the optimal selection because the search space is tiny (≤8 triplets + ≤12 pairs + singles).

Selection objective:
- choose **0, 1, or 2** hypotheses
- **no 2D observation used twice**
- maximize total score (possibly with a penalty for using only 2 views instead of 3).

This “small ILP / brute force” step is the missing piece that makes the method robust and unambiguous.

## 4) Identity assignment: your voting works, but add one anchor-based rule to prevent systematic flips
Your segmentation-weight voting is a good *local* cue, but it will fail exactly in the regime you care about (strong occlusions, tails crossing), where votes are weak/ambiguous.

A very effective stabilizer is:
1) Solve **anchor parts first**: `head` + `tail_root` (they’re usually most stable).
2) Use them to assign mouse identity by **temporal continuity** (nearest-neighbor in 3D from previous frame, or a 2-state Viterbi over “swap / no swap”).
3) Assign all other bodyparts in that frame by:
   - segmentation vote if decisive,
   - otherwise closeness to the anchor-defined body axis / anchor centroid.

This reduces identity switching without relying on “majority of parts,” which can be wrong when many parts are missing/ambiguous.

## 5) Lonely parts: your “majority of previous DLC-assigned parts” is reasonable, but apply it as a *per-camera mapping*
A subtle but important point: DLC identity confusion often happens **independently per camera**. So for a lonely observation in camera `cam2_front`, using a global “DLC assignment majority” across all cameras can inject errors.

Instead, compute for each frame and each camera \(c\) a mapping:
\[
\text{map}_c(\text{DLC individual label}) \rightarrow \text{mouse ID}
\]
estimated from all *non-lonely* bodyparts in that camera/frame. Then apply \(\text{map}_c\) to lonely parts in that camera. This respects the reality that swaps happen per view.

## 6) Residual thresholding: estimate noise robustly (MAD), then use DOF-aware gating
Your plan to adapt thresholds from residual statistics is good, but:
- use a **robust scale estimator** (MAD or trimmed RMS) so wrong associations don’t inflate sigma;
- gate using:
  - RMS px threshold per camera, or
  - \(\chi^2\) with DOF = \(2n_{views}-3\) for a single 3D point.

A clean workflow:
1) bootstrap with a conservative fixed threshold (e.g., 5–10 px),
2) collect accepted hypotheses,
3) compute per-camera robust \(\hat{\sigma}_{pix}\),
4) set acceptance threshold like \( \text{RMS} < 3\hat{\sigma}_{pix}\) (or chi-square quantile).

## 7) Notes on your current Ceres codebase vs what you want to build
- Your environment/build setup is solid (Ceres, Eigen, pybind11 in conda; CMake + Ninja build). fileciteturn0file0turn0file1turn0file2
- Right now the C++ module implements a **model-based BA** (`solve`) with mouse poses, template points, slack, spline priors etc. fileciteturn0file5turn0file6
- The Python script `baPointsOnlyCeres.py` calls `mouse_ba.solve_points_only(...)`, but that function does **not** exist in the shown `mouse_ba_module.cpp` (it exports only `solve`). So the “points-only” path is currently structurally inconsistent and will need either:
  - a new exported function `solve_points_only`, or
  - adjusting the Python to call `solve` with a degenerate model (not what you want). fileciteturn0file3turn0file6

For your triangulation/cleaning algorithm, you want a **much simpler Ceres problem**:
- parameter block: a single 3D point \(P_w\),
- residual blocks: reprojection errors for each included 2D observation,
- optional robust loss,
- weights derived from DLC likelihood (your existing sigma-from-likelihood idea is reusable). fileciteturn0file6

That simplicity is a big win: fast solves, easy diagnostics, and clean acceptance criteria.

## A few concrete questions that affect design choices
1) Are your images already undistorted? `cameras.json` has only fx,fy,cx,cy and no distortion model. fileciteturn0file8  
2) Do you expect systematic sync offsets between cameras (even 1–2 frames)? If yes, you need to allow temporal offset hypotheses or pre-align.
3) How exactly will segmentation weights be provided: precomputed per (frame, camera, pixel) mask labels, or as already-aggregated per DLC point?

If you answer those, I can help you lock down the scoring/gating rules so the later implementation is straightforward and testable.

Assistant: Alright — with your clarifications, the clean separation becomes:

- **Stage A (pure geometry):** decide which 2D observations across cameras belong to the *same* physical 3D point for a given bodypart, **without using segmentation** (and optionally without DLC likelihood).
- **Stage B (identity):** assign the resulting 3D points (and any leftover 2D-only “lonely” parts) to **mouse 0 vs mouse 1**, using segmentation weights + anchors + temporal continuity + your “DLC-group majority” fallback.

Below is a concrete, systematic pipeline that matches what you want, while keeping it implementable and testable.

---

## Stage A — Geometry-only multi-view association per frame & bodypart

### A1) Inputs per frame, per bodypart \(b\)
For each camera \(c \in \{\text{top, front, side}\}\), DLC provides up to two candidates:
\[
o_{c,0}=(u,v),\quad o_{c,1}=(u,v)
\]
(each may be missing).

Let \(O\) be the set of all available observations among these up to 6 points.

### A2) Hypothesis generation (triplets, then pairs, then singles)
Generate hypotheses **ignoring identities**:

- **Triplets:** choose one observation from each camera:  
  \[
  H = \{o_{\text{top},i}, o_{\text{front},j}, o_{\text{side},k}\},\; i,j,k\in\{0,1\}
  \]
  ⇒ up to \(2^3=8\) triplets, minus missing points.
- **Pairs:** all 3 camera pairs × (2×2) choices ⇒ up to 12 pairs.
- **Singles:** any remaining unused observations can remain as “single-ray” items (no triangulation).

### A3) Cheap geometric gates (before Ceres)
For each triplet/pair hypothesis, apply your agreed gates (and I’d add one extra that’s very cheap and strong):

**Gate 0 (optional but recommended): epipolar distance**
- For each camera pair within the hypothesis, compute distance of one point to the other’s epipolar line. Reject if > \(e_{\text{epi}}\) (a few pixels).
- This costs almost nothing and removes many wrong pairings before ray math.

**Gate 1: ray-angle**
- Reject if smallest angle between any ray pair < \(\theta_{\min}\).

**Gate 2: closest-approach distance (pairwise)**
- For each camera pair in the hypothesis, compute minimum distance between rays; reject if > \(d_{\max}\).

**Gate 3: cage bounding volume**
- Triangulate a quick initial 3D point (pair midpoint method) and reject if outside plausible volume.

**Gate 4: fast reprojection**
- Using the initial 3D guess, reproject to involved cameras; reject if any error > \(e_{\text{init}}\).

Only survivors go to Ceres.

### A4) Ceres “single-point BA” refinement and geometric score
For each surviving hypothesis \(H\):

- Unknown: one 3D point \(P\).
- Residuals: reprojection residuals \((\Delta u, \Delta v)\) in each participating view.
- Optional: robust loss (Huber/Cauchy) to reduce sensitivity if a single view is slightly off.

**Score (geometry-only):**
Use either RMS pixel error or chi-square form with \(\sigma_{\text{pix}}\). Since you want bootstrapping:
- Start with a user parameter \(e_{\text{init}}\) (e.g., 5–10 px) to accept initial inliers.
- From accepted hypotheses, estimate \(\sigma_{\text{pix}}\) robustly (MAD / trimmed RMS), per camera if you want.
- Then accept hypotheses by:
  - RMS < \(k\sigma_{\text{pix}}\), or
  - \(\chi^2\) threshold with DOF \(=2n_{\text{views}}-3\).

**DLC likelihood weighting:** make it a switch.
- If enabled: map DLC likelihood to per-observation \(\sigma\) or to a weight in the residual.
- If disabled: all observations have equal weight.

### A5) Disjoint selection (brute force)
Now you’ll have a small set of “valid” triplets/pairs with scores.

Goal: pick **up to two** hypotheses (two mice) such that:
- no 2D observation is used more than once (disjointness),
- total geometric score is maximized,
- optionally prefer triplets over pairs via a small bonus/penalty term.

Because the candidate set is tiny, brute force is trivial:
- Evaluate all combinations of {0, 1, 2} hypotheses that are disjoint.
- Keep best.

**Output of Stage A (per frame, per bodypart):**
- 0, 1, or 2 reconstructed 3D points (each tied to the set of 2D observations used),
- plus a set of leftover “lonely” 2D observations not used anywhere.

Importantly: at this point you have *two unlabeled* 3D points (“A” and “B”), not mouse0/mouse1 yet.

---

## Stage B — Identity assignment (uses segmentation + anchors + temporal continuity)

### B1) Segmentation weights per 2D observation
As you described, compute for every available DLC point:
- take a window (circle or square),
- apply Gaussian weighting (σ, radius rule-of-thumb),
- count labels: background, mouse0-seg, mouse1-seg,
- produce weights \(w_{\text{bg}}, w_0, w_1\).

These are **not used** in Stage A, only here.

### B2) Vote / evidence for a reconstructed 3D point
For a 3D point hypothesis \(H\) (triplet or pair), accumulate segmentation evidence from its member observations:
\[
V_0(H)=\sum_{o\in H} f(w_0(o)),\quad
V_1(H)=\sum_{o\in H} f(w_1(o))
\]
Where \(f\) can be:
- identity: \(f(x)=x\),
- or your “positive vote if >0” rule (effectively a thresholded version).

I’d still recommend keeping it *soft* (use weights) and only fall back to hard votes when you need to.

### B3) Anchor-driven swap/no-swap decision per frame
To suppress identity switching, treat identity as a **binary swap state** per frame.

Use anchors (head + tail-root) because they’re stable:
1) From Stage A, get the two 3D candidates for head and tail-root (if present).
2) For each of the two possible assignments (swap / no swap), compute cost:
   - temporal continuity cost from previous frame (distance in 3D for anchors),
   - plus segmentation evidence term (optional, weakly weighted).
3) Choose the lower-cost assignment.

This yields a consistent mapping “point A → mouse0 or mouse1” for the frame (or for a short window if you later want smoothing).

If anchors are missing/degenerate in a frame, you can fall back to:
- segmentation vote majority across available parts,
- or carry-forward last reliable assignment.

### B4) Assign all other 3D points using (1) segmentation if decisive, else (2) body-axis proximity
For each bodypart’s unlabeled 3D points:
- If segmentation evidence is decisive (e.g., \(V_0\) clearly > \(V_1\)), assign directly.
- If ambiguous:
  - compute mouse centroids / body axes from assigned anchors,
  - assign by proximity to the corresponding mouse’s anchor-defined body axis / centroid,
  - and keep temporal continuity (don’t flip without strong reason).

This is exactly the “segmentation vote → else anchor-axis” rule you endorsed.

### B5) Lonely parts (2D-only leftovers): your “DLC-group majority” as a mapping
Now the key subtlety you clarified:

For a lonely 2D observation \(o_{c,d}\) (camera \(c\), DLC identity label \(d\)), you don’t want to trust DLC directly. Instead:

1) Consider the set of **other bodyparts** in the same frame & camera that had the **same DLC label \(d\)** and that *did* get a confident mouse assignment by Stage B so far.
2) Take the majority (or weighted majority) of their **new** mouse assignments.
3) Assign the lonely observation accordingly.

This is equivalent to estimating, per frame & camera, a mapping:
\[
\text{map}_{c}(d)\in\{\text{mouse0, mouse1}\}
\]
from already-resolved parts, and applying it to unresolved ones — which prevents DLC’s internal contradictions from propagating.

If even that mapping is undefined (no resolved parts with that DLC label in that camera):
- use segmentation weights of the lonely observation if informative,
- else use temporal continuity from the last frame where that bodypart was confidently assigned.

---

## What you end up with
Per frame:
- For each bodypart: up to two 3D points, assigned to mouse0/mouse1 (or missing).
- For any bodypart not triangulated: at least a 2D assignment per camera based on the mapping + segmentation fallback.
- Identity switching is suppressed by the anchor + continuity swap model.

---

## Two design “knobs” worth making explicit
1) **Acceptance thresholds:** \(e_{\text{init}}, \theta_{\min}, d_{\max}, e_{\text{epi}}\) — and the robust bootstrap loop that converts \(e_{\text{init}}\) into calibrated \(\sigma_{\text{pix}}\).
2) **How decisive is “decisive”:** segmentation evidence difference threshold (or your “>0” rule), and how strongly continuity can override ambiguous segmentation.

---

## One suggestion that will save pain later
Log (per frame/part) a compact diagnostic record:
- which hypotheses were tested,
- which gates failed,
- BA residual summary,
- final selected hypothesis(es),
- identity evidence \(V_0,V_1\) and whether anchor/continuity overrode it.

When something goes wrong, this makes it debuggable in minutes rather than days.

---

Assistant: Below is a concrete **per-frame pseudocode skeleton**. It’s organized so you can implement it literally, and it separates:

- **Stage A (geometry-only association + triangulation selection)**  
- **Stage B (identity assignment + lonely-part resolution)**

I’ll write it “per frame” and “per bodypart”, with explicit hypothesis enumeration, gating, BA scoring, disjoint selection, then identity/anchors.

## Data model (minimal)

```text
CAMS = ["top","front","side"]
DLC_IDS = [0,1]
BODYPARTS = ["nose", "earL", ...]  # 10 parts

Obs:
  cam: str
  dlc_id: 0|1
  uv: (u,v)
  conf: float  # DLC likelihood, optional usage
  seg_w: (w_bg, w_m0, w_m1)  # computed later; not used in Stage A

Hypothesis:
  obs_list: list[Obs]  # size 3 (triplet) or 2 (pair)
  views: list[cam]
  initial_P: 3D
  refined_P: 3D
  reproj_stats: {rms_px, max_px, chi2, per_view_residuals}
  score_geom: float

TriangulatedItem:
  P: 3D or None
  obs_list: list[Obs]  # the used obs
  kind: "triplet"|"pair"|"single"
  geom_ok: bool
  # later:
  mouse_id: 0|1|None
  vote: (v0,v1)  # identity votes
```

## Helper functions (signatures)

```text
build_observations(frame, bodypart) -> list[Obs]
  # returns up to 6 obs (3 cams × 2 dlc individuals), skipping missing

compute_seg_weights(obs, seg_masks, r, sigma) -> (w_bg, w_m0, w_m1)
  # windowed Gaussian counting around obs.uv

epipolar_gate(obs_a, obs_b, cam_a, cam_b, epi_thresh_px) -> bool

ray_angle_gate(obs_list, cameras) -> bool

closest_approach_gate_pair(obs_a, obs_b, cameras, d_max) -> bool

bbox_gate(P_init, cage_bbox) -> bool

fast_reproj_gate(P_init, obs_list, cameras, e_init_px) -> bool

pair_midpoint_init(obs_a, obs_b, cameras) -> P_init

run_ceres_point_ba(P_init, obs_list, cameras, sigma_pix, use_dlc_weighting) -> (P_refined, reproj_stats)

geom_score(reproj_stats, sigma_pix) -> float  # larger is better (e.g. -chi2)

select_best_disjoint(hypotheses_valid, max_points=2) -> list[Hypothesis]

positive_vote(seg_w, thr=0.01) -> (v0,v1)
  v0 = 1 if w_m0 > thr else 0
  v1 = 1 if w_m1 > thr else 0
  return (v0,v1)

anchor_swap_decision(prev_state, anchors_now, seg_votes_now, params) -> swap|noswap|unknown

assign_by_axis_or_centroid(P, mouse0_model, mouse1_model) -> 0|1
  # distance to anchor-defined axis/centroid etc.

estimate_cam_mapping_from_resolved(resolved_items_in_cam) -> map: dlc_id -> mouse_id or None

resolve_lonely_obs(obs, cam_map, seg_w, prev_assignments, params) -> mouse_id or None
```

---

## Main per-frame pipeline pseudocode

```text
function process_frame(frame_t, dlc_data, cameras, seg_masks, prev_frame_state, params):

  results = dict()  # results[bodypart] = list[TriangulatedItem] (0..2 + singles)

  # ---------- Stage A: geometry-only association ----------
  for each bodypart b in BODYPARTS:

    O = build_observations(frame_t, b)  # up to 6 Obs
    if O is empty:
      results[b] = []
      continue

    # A2) generate triplet hypotheses
    triplet_candidates = []
    for i in DLC_IDS:
      for j in DLC_IDS:
        for k in DLC_IDS:
          obs_top   = find Obs in O with (cam="top",   dlc_id=i)
          obs_front = find Obs in O with (cam="front", dlc_id=j)
          obs_side  = find Obs in O with (cam="side",  dlc_id=k)
          if any missing -> continue
          triplet_candidates.append([obs_top, obs_front, obs_side])

    # A2) generate pair hypotheses (all cam pairs, all dlc_id combos)
    pair_candidates = []
    for (camA, camB) in [("top","front"),("top","side"),("front","side")]:
      for i in DLC_IDS:
        for j in DLC_IDS:
          obsA = find Obs in O with (cam=camA, dlc_id=i)
          obsB = find Obs in O with (cam=camB, dlc_id=j)
          if any missing -> continue
          pair_candidates.append([obsA, obsB])

    valid_hypotheses = []

    # A3-A4) evaluate triplets first
    for obs_list in triplet_candidates:

      # Gate 0: epipolar (pairwise within triplet)
      if not epipolar_gate(obs_list[0], obs_list[1], ..., params.epi_thresh): continue
      if not epipolar_gate(obs_list[0], obs_list[2], ..., params.epi_thresh): continue
      if not epipolar_gate(obs_list[1], obs_list[2], ..., params.epi_thresh): continue

      # Gate 1: ray angles
      if not ray_angle_gate(obs_list, cameras, params.theta_min): continue

      # Gate 2: closest-approach distances (pairwise)
      if not closest_approach_gate_pair(obs_list[0], obs_list[1], cameras, params.d_max): continue
      if not closest_approach_gate_pair(obs_list[0], obs_list[2], cameras, params.d_max): continue
      if not closest_approach_gate_pair(obs_list[1], obs_list[2], cameras, params.d_max): continue

      # Init from best-conditioned pair (largest ray angle)
      (obs_a, obs_b) = choose_pair_with_max_ray_angle(obs_list, cameras)
      P_init = pair_midpoint_init(obs_a, obs_b, cameras)

      # Gate 3: bbox
      if not bbox_gate(P_init, params.cage_bbox): continue

      # Gate 4: fast reprojection
      if not fast_reproj_gate(P_init, obs_list, cameras, params.e_init_px): continue

      # BA refine
      (P_ref, reproj_stats) = run_ceres_point_ba(
                                P_init, obs_list, cameras,
                                sigma_pix=params.sigma_pix_current,
                                use_dlc_weighting=params.use_dlc_weighting)

      # Accept by current thresholding rule
      if reproj_stats.rms_px > params.accept_rms_px: continue
      # optionally: chi2 threshold using DOF=2*3-3=3

      h = Hypothesis(obs_list=obs_list, initial_P=P_init, refined_P=P_ref,
                     reproj_stats=reproj_stats,
                     score_geom=geom_score(reproj_stats, params.sigma_pix_current))
      valid_hypotheses.append(h)

    # A3-A4) evaluate pairs (for later fallback)
    for obs_list in pair_candidates:

      # Gate 0: epipolar
      if not epipolar_gate(obs_list[0], obs_list[1], ..., params.epi_thresh): continue

      # Gate 1: ray angle
      if ray_angle(obs_list[0], obs_list[1], cameras) < params.theta_min_pair: continue

      # Gate 2: closest approach
      if not closest_approach_gate_pair(obs_list[0], obs_list[1], cameras, params.d_max): continue

      P_init = pair_midpoint_init(obs_list[0], obs_list[1], cameras)

      # Gate 3: bbox
      if not bbox_gate(P_init, params.cage_bbox): continue

      # Gate 4: fast reproj
      if not fast_reproj_gate(P_init, obs_list, cameras, params.e_init_px): continue

      (P_ref, reproj_stats) = run_ceres_point_ba(
                                P_init, obs_list, cameras,
                                sigma_pix=params.sigma_pix_current,
                                use_dlc_weighting=params.use_dlc_weighting)

      if reproj_stats.rms_px > params.accept_rms_px_pair: continue

      h = Hypothesis(...score_geom=geom_score(...))
      valid_hypotheses.append(h)

    # A5) disjoint selection: choose up to two hypotheses
    chosen = select_best_disjoint(valid_hypotheses, max_points=2)

    used_obs = union of obs in chosen
    items = []

    for h in chosen:
      items.append(TriangulatedItem(P=h.refined_P, obs_list=h.obs_list,
                                   kind=("triplet" if len(h.obs_list)==3 else "pair"),
                                   geom_ok=True))

    # leftover singles (not triangulated)
    for obs in O:
      if obs not in used_obs:
        items.append(TriangulatedItem(P=None, obs_list=[obs], kind="single", geom_ok=False))

    results[b] = items

  # Optional: bootstrap sigma_pix update after some frames or after first pass
  # Collect reproj residuals from all geom_ok items and update params.sigma_pix_current robustly.

  # ---------- Stage B: compute segmentation weights for all observations ----------
  # (still per frame)
  for each bodypart b in BODYPARTS:
    for item in results[b]:
      for obs in item.obs_list:
        if obs.seg_w not computed:
          obs.seg_w = compute_seg_weights(obs, seg_masks[obs.cam][frame_t], params.r, params.sigma)

  # ---------- Stage B: identity assignment using anchors + continuity ----------
  # B3) determine swap/no-swap using anchors if possible
  anchors = ["head", "tail_root"]  # adapt to your labels
  anchors_now = extract triangulated items for anchors that have 2 points (or 1 point)
  swap_state = anchor_swap_decision(prev_frame_state.swap_state, anchors_now, results, params)

  # B4) assign mouse_id for each bodypart’s triangulated 3D points
  # Strategy:
  #  - if two points exist for a bodypart: assign both (one to each mouse) using swap_state + evidence
  #  - if one point exists: assign to mouse0 or mouse1 based on decisive votes; else axis/centroid; else continuity

  # First build anchor-defined models for mouse0/mouse1 in this frame
  mouse_models = build_mouse_models_from_assigned_anchors(results, swap_state, prev_frame_state, params)
  # includes centroid/axis and predicted positions from previous frame

  for each bodypart b:
    items = results[b]

    # compute votes for each item (triplet/pair/single)
    for item in items:
      (v0, v1) = (0,0)
      for obs in item.obs_list:
        (dv0, dv1) = positive_vote(obs.seg_w, thr=params.vote_thr)  # default thr=0.01
        v0 += dv0
        v1 += dv1
      item.vote = (v0, v1)

    # Separate triangulated points (P exists) from singles
    points3D = [it for it in items if it.P is not None]
    singles  = [it for it in items if it.P is None]

    if len(points3D) == 2:
      # Two unlabeled points: decide which is mouse0 vs mouse1
      # Use: (a) swap_state if anchor-linked, else (b) votes, else (c) axis/centroid proximity, else (d) continuity
      assign_two_points(points3D, mouse_models, swap_state, params)

    elif len(points3D) == 1:
      # One point: assign to best mouse
      it = points3D[0]
      if decisive(it.vote, params):  # e.g. v0 != v1 and max(v0,v1) > 0
        it.mouse_id = argmax(it.vote)
      else:
        it.mouse_id = assign_by_axis_or_centroid(it.P, mouse_models.m0, mouse_models.m1)
        # if still ambiguous, use continuity (closest to prev position for that bodypart)

    # singles remain unassigned for now (handled in B5)

  # ---------- B5: resolve lonely singles using per-camera DLC-label mapping ----------
  # Build per-camera mapping from already-resolved items using your rule:
  # mapping is inferred from NEW assignments among parts that share the same DLC label in that camera.
  cam_maps = dict()
  for cam in CAMS:
    resolved_obs = []
    for b in BODYPARTS:
      for item in results[b]:
        if item.mouse_id is not None:
          for obs in item.obs_list:
            if obs.cam == cam:
              resolved_obs.append((obs.dlc_id, item.mouse_id))
    cam_maps[cam] = estimate_cam_mapping_from_resolved(resolved_obs)
      # e.g., for each dlc_id choose majority mouse_id

  # Apply mapping to singles
  for each bodypart b:
    for item in results[b]:
      if item.kind == "single":
        obs = item.obs_list[0]
        mapped = cam_maps[obs.cam].get(obs.dlc_id)  # may be None
        if mapped is not None:
          item.mouse_id = mapped
        else:
          # fallback: segmentation vote if decisive, else continuity
          (v0, v1) = positive_vote(obs.seg_w, thr=params.vote_thr)
          if v0 != v1 and (v0+v1) > 0:
            item.mouse_id = 0 if v0>v1 else 1
          else:
            item.mouse_id = continuity_fallback_for_single(obs, prev_frame_state, params)

  # Done for this frame
  frame_state = update_state_for_next_frame(results, swap_state, params)
  return results, frame_state
```

---

## Notes on key subroutines (so implementation is unambiguous)

### `select_best_disjoint(valid_hypotheses, max_points=2)`
Brute force is easiest:

```text
best = []
best_score = -inf

# consider selecting 0, 1, or 2 hypotheses
for H1 in [None] + valid_hypotheses:
  for H2 in [None] + valid_hypotheses:
    chosen = unique non-None in {H1,H2}
    if len(chosen) > max_points: continue
    if not disjoint_obs(chosen): continue
    score = sum(h.score_geom for h in chosen) + bonus(chosen)
    if score > best_score:
      best = chosen; best_score = score

return best
```

Bonus example: +λ for each triplet, 0 for pair, to slightly prefer 3-view solutions.

### `decisive(vote, params)`
With your default rule:
- each contributing obs can vote for mouse0 if \(w_0>0.01\), similarly for mouse1.
- decisive if one side strictly larger.

```text
decisive((v0,v1)):
  return (v0 != v1) and (max(v0,v1) > 0)
```

### `assign_two_points(points3D, mouse_models, swap_state, params)`
Compute assignment cost for the two possibilities:

- Option A: P_a→mouse0, P_b→mouse1
- Option B: P_a→mouse1, P_b→mouse0

Cost terms:
- negative of votes (if votes decisive / informative)
- distance to anchor axis/centroid
- temporal continuity (distance to previous frame’s same bodypart position)

Pick lower cost. Use `swap_state` as a prior/penalty (i.e., discourage flipping unless cost gain exceeds threshold).

---

## What you can implement first (smallest working vertical slice)
1) Stage A with:
   - triplet enumeration,
   - gates 1–4 (skip epipolar if you want initially),
   - point-only BA,
   - disjoint selection.
2) Stage B with just:
   - segmentation vote,
   - then anchors+continuity (swap/no-swap).

Then add lonely-part mapping and bootstrapped σ.

If one mouse occludes the other, e.g. an ear tip in front of a mouse's belly would be assigned to the belly id and not to the ear tip id. So we need to be open for both ids. Assistant: You’re reading my earlier `decisive((v0,v1))` correctly: it would “collapse” ambiguity by picking the side with the larger vote count. That’s **not** what you want, and your reasoning (extremal parts + convex silhouette + occlusion causing “belly label wins”) is solid.

### Replace “decisive” with “exclusive support” (your intended behavior)
What you described is:

- Each *observation* can vote for **mouse0**, **mouse1**, **both**, or **none**, based on thresholding the segmentation neighborhood weights.
- If both are plausible (both weights above threshold), you explicitly want **neutrality** (a vote for both), and let geometry + other views + anchors resolve later.

So don’t use a function that picks a winner from `(v0,v1)`. Use a function that only decides when segmentation is **exclusive**.

#### Observation-level voting (default)
Let `thr = 0.01` (normalized weights). For one observation `obs.seg_w = (w_bg, w0, w1)`:

```text
obs_vote(w0, w1, thr):
  dv0 = 1 if w0 > thr else 0
  dv1 = 1 if w1 > thr else 0
  return (dv0, dv1)
```

This naturally yields:
- (1,0): supports mouse0 only
- (0,1): supports mouse1 only
- (1,1): ambiguous / neutral (your desired case)
- (0,0): no information

#### Item-level aggregation (triplet/pair/single)
For an item (triangulated or single), sum votes over its observations.

#### “Exclusive support” decision
```text
exclusive_mouse_id(v0, v1):
  if v0 > 0 and v1 == 0: return 0
  if v1 > 0 and v0 == 0: return 1
  return None  # ambiguous or no support
```

Then in Stage B you only *directly* assign mouse_id from segmentation when `exclusive_mouse_id(...)` returns 0 or 1. Otherwise you defer to:
- anchor swap/continuity
- axis/centroid proximity
- temporal continuity per bodypart

This matches your “be open for both ids” requirement.

---

## What does `max_points=2` mean?
It’s the constraint:

> per frame, per bodypart, there can be **at most two physical instances** of that bodypart (because there are two mice).

So in Stage A (geometry-only), after generating and scoring all triplet/pair hypotheses, the disjoint-selection step is allowed to choose:
- **0** hypotheses (bodypart not reliably observed),
- **1** hypothesis (only one mouse visible / other occluded),
- **2** hypotheses (both mice visible),

but never more than 2.

That’s what `max_points=2` enforces.

---

## What are `P_a` and `P_b`, and why “two possibilities” for assignment cost?
After Stage A, for a given bodypart in a frame, you may have selected **two unlabeled 3D points**. Call them:

- `P_a` = the first selected 3D reconstruction (from some triplet/pair)
- `P_b` = the second selected 3D reconstruction

At that moment, they are **not** mouse0/mouse1 yet — just “two candidates”.

Since there are two mice, there are exactly **two identity assignments**:

1) `P_a → mouse0` and `P_b → mouse1`  
2) `P_a → mouse1` and `P_b → mouse0`

The “assignment cost” is simply a way to choose between these two labelings using:
- anchor-based swap/no-swap state (global per frame)
- temporal continuity (distance to previous frame’s mouse0/mouse1 for that bodypart)
- segmentation votes **only as weak / exclusive evidence** (with your ambiguity preserved)

So `P_a` and `P_b` are not special geometrically; they’re just the two selected points for that bodypart, and “two possibilities” is just the inherent swap symmetry.

---

## Minimal pseudocode patch for the identity part
Replace the earlier “decisive” logic with:

```text
# after computing item.vote = (v0,v1)
item.exclusive = exclusive_mouse_id(v0,v1)  # 0,1, or None
```

Then for the case of two points:

```text
assign_two_points(points3D=[A,B]):

  # if segmentation is exclusive and consistent, use it
  if A.exclusive == 0 and B.exclusive in {1,None}: prefer A->0, B->1 (unless continuity strongly disagrees)
  if A.exclusive == 1 and B.exclusive in {0,None}: prefer A->1, B->0
  if B.exclusive is not None and A.exclusive is None: assign B, other gets remaining mouse (softly)

  # otherwise (both ambiguous / no support):
  choose between (A->0,B->1) vs (A->1,B->0) by continuity + anchor swap prior + axis proximity
```

This preserves your “vote for both if both plausible” behavior.

Assistant: Below is **Stage B rewritten** to match your intended semantics:

- segmentation votes are **non-committal by default** (a point may vote for both mice),
- **only “exclusive support”** triggers a direct segmentation-based assignment,
- otherwise identity is resolved by **anchors + temporal continuity**, and if still ambiguous by **axis/centroid proximity**,
- lonely 2D observations get assigned via your **“same DLC-label group majority of new assignments”** mapping (per camera).

I’ll assume Stage A already produced, for each bodypart, a set of items:
- up to 2 triangulated items with 3D point \(P\),
- plus possible singles (no 3D).

---

## Stage B pseudocode (per frame)

```text
function stageB_assign_identities(frame_t, results_stageA, seg_masks, prev_state, params):

  # params.vote_thr default = 0.01
  # params use: r, sigma for seg window; continuity weights; axis weights; etc.

  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  # B1) Compute segmentation weights + observation-level votes
  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  for each bodypart b:
    for each item in results_stageA[b]:
      for each obs in item.obs_list:
        if obs.seg_w not computed:
          obs.seg_w = compute_seg_weights(obs, seg_masks[obs.cam][frame_t],
                                          params.r, params.sigma)

        # observation vote: can be (1,0), (0,1), (1,1), (0,0)
        (dv0, dv1) = obs_vote(obs.seg_w.w0, obs.seg_w.w1, params.vote_thr)
        obs.vote = (dv0, dv1)

      # item vote = sum of obs votes
      item.vote = (sum(obs.vote.v0 for obs in item.obs_list),
                   sum(obs.vote.v1 for obs in item.obs_list))

      # EXCLUSIVE evidence only (otherwise None)
      item.exclusive = exclusive_mouse_id(item.vote.v0, item.vote.v1)
      # exclusive_mouse_id:
      #   if v0>0 and v1==0 -> 0
      #   if v1>0 and v0==0 -> 1
      #   else -> None  (ambiguous or no info)

  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  # B2) Determine global swap/no-swap for this frame using anchors
  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  # Anchors should be parts like head + tail_root (whatever labels you use)
  anchor_parts = params.anchor_parts  # e.g. ["head","tail_root"]
  anchors_now = extract_anchor_3D_candidates(results_stageA, anchor_parts)
  # anchors_now could contain up to two 3D points per anchor part (unlabeled)

  # Decide swap state:
  # swap_state in {NOSWAP, SWAP, UNKNOWN}
  # - primary signal: temporal continuity on anchor positions
  # - secondary: exclusive segmentation evidence on anchors (weak; only if exclusive)
  swap_state = decide_swap_state(prev_state, anchors_now, params)
  # If anchors missing or degenerate, swap_state may be UNKNOWN.

  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  # B3) Build per-mouse geometric "models" from anchors for disambiguation
  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  # This yields for each mouse:
  # - anchor centroid
  # - anchor axis (e.g. head->tail_root vector)
  # - predicted positions from previous frame (optional)
  mouse_model = build_mouse_models(prev_state, anchors_now, swap_state, params)

  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  # B4) Assign identities for triangulated items (3D points)
  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  for each bodypart b:

    items = results_stageA[b]
    points3D = [it for it in items if it.P is not None]
    singles  = [it for it in items if it.P is None]

    if len(points3D) == 2:
      A = points3D[0]; B = points3D[1]

      # Evaluate two assignments: (A->0,B->1) vs (A->1,B->0)
      cost01 = assignment_cost(A, 0, b, mouse_model, prev_state, swap_state, params) \
            + assignment_cost(B, 1, b, mouse_model, prev_state, swap_state, params)
      cost10 = assignment_cost(A, 1, b, mouse_model, prev_state, swap_state, params) \
            + assignment_cost(B, 0, b, mouse_model, prev_state, swap_state, params)

      if cost01 <= cost10:
        A.mouse_id = 0; B.mouse_id = 1
      else:
        A.mouse_id = 1; B.mouse_id = 0

    elif len(points3D) == 1:
      A = points3D[0]

      # If exclusive segmentation evidence exists, use it (only then)
      if A.exclusive is not None:
        A.mouse_id = A.exclusive
      else:
        # Otherwise pick the identity minimizing cost (continuity + axis proximity + swap prior)
        c0 = assignment_cost(A, 0, b, mouse_model, prev_state, swap_state, params)
        c1 = assignment_cost(A, 1, b, mouse_model, prev_state, swap_state, params)
        A.mouse_id = 0 if c0 <= c1 else 1

    # (Do nothing for singles here; handled later)

  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  # B5) Create per-camera mapping from DLC label -> mouse_id (from NEW assignments)
  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  cam_map = dict()
  for cam in CAMS:
    # gather resolved observations in this camera:
    pairs = []  # list of (dlc_id, mouse_id)
    for each bodypart b:
      for each item in results_stageA[b]:
        if item.mouse_id is None: continue
        for obs in item.obs_list:
          if obs.cam == cam:
            pairs.append((obs.dlc_id, item.mouse_id))

    cam_map[cam] = estimate_mapping_majority(pairs)
    # estimate_mapping_majority:
    #   for dlc_id in {0,1}:
    #     count mouse0 vs mouse1 among pairs with that dlc_id
    #     if strict majority -> map[dlc_id]=winner else map[dlc_id]=None

  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  # B6) Assign identities for single-ray items ("lonely parts")
  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  for each bodypart b:
    for each item in results_stageA[b]:
      if item.kind != "single": continue
      obs = item.obs_list[0]

      # First: use mapping inferred from other parts that shared the SAME DLC label in this camera
      mapped = cam_map[obs.cam].get(obs.dlc_id)
      if mapped is not None:
        item.mouse_id = mapped
        continue

      # Second: use exclusive segmentation evidence (ONLY if exclusive)
      # Here item.vote is computed already from obs.vote
      if item.exclusive is not None:
        item.mouse_id = item.exclusive
        continue

      # Third: temporal continuity fallback (bodypart-specific if you track it)
      item.mouse_id = continuity_fallback_single(obs, b, prev_state, params)
      # if even this fails, leave as None

  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  # B7) Update state for next frame (store assigned 3D positions, swap_state, etc.)
  # ------------------------------------------------------------
  new_state = update_state(prev_state, results_stageA, swap_state, params)

  return results_stageA, new_state
```

---

## Key subroutines (precise behavior)

### Observation vote + exclusive rule (your default)
```text
obs_vote(w0, w1, thr=0.01):
  dv0 = 1 if w0 > thr else 0
  dv1 = 1 if w1 > thr else 0
  return (dv0, dv1)

exclusive_mouse_id(v0, v1):
  if v0 > 0 and v1 == 0: return 0
  if v1 > 0 and v0 == 0: return 1
  return None
```

This makes `(1,1)` explicitly *non-decisive* and keeps neutrality.

---

## The assignment cost (what it should contain)
This cost is only used when segmentation is ambiguous/non-exclusive.

```text
assignment_cost(item, mouse_id, bodypart, mouse_model, prev_state, swap_state, params):

  cost = 0

  # 1) Swap/no-swap prior (weak): discourage violating the frame’s swap decision
  if swap_state != UNKNOWN:
    cost += swap_penalty(item, mouse_id, swap_state, params)

  # 2) Temporal continuity (strong for anchors, moderate otherwise)
  if item.P is not None:
    P_prev = prev_state.get_3D(bodypart, mouse_id)  # may be None
    if P_prev exists:
      cost += params.w_cont * || item.P - P_prev ||^2

  # 3) Anchor axis / centroid proximity (moderate)
  if item.P is not None and mouse_model[mouse_id] exists:
    cost += params.w_axis * distance_to_mouse_axis(item.P, mouse_model[mouse_id].axis)^2
    cost += params.w_cent * || item.P - mouse_model[mouse_id].centroid ||^2

  # 4) Exclusive segmentation evidence (optional and weak; but note: exclusive handled earlier)
  # If you want, you can add a tiny term using vote difference, but only if exclusive.
  # Otherwise keep it out.

  return cost
```

### Swap decision using anchors
You can implement `decide_swap_state` as a two-hypothesis test:

- Hypothesis NOSWAP: current anchor point A corresponds to previous mouse0, B to mouse1
- Hypothesis SWAP: A corresponds to previous mouse1, B to mouse0

Compute continuity costs over available anchors (head, tail_root), pick smaller, but only commit if margin exceeds a threshold; else UNKNOWN.

---

## What changed vs my earlier version
- No “winner-takes-all” from segmentation unless **exclusive**.
- Ambiguity `(1,1)` is preserved and pushed to geometry/continuity resolution.
- Singles (lonely) are assigned primarily via your **new-assignment majority within same DLC-label group**, per camera.

Concretely, replace B6 with:

```text
function assign_single(item, bodypart b):

  obs = item.obs_list[0]

  # 1) segmentation decisive if exclusive
  if item.exclusive is not None:
    item.mouse_id = item.exclusive
    return

  # 2) segmentation has NO result at all -> use DLC-label group mapping
  # "no result" means: v0==0 AND v1==0 (not ambiguous (1,1), but truly none)
  (v0, v1) = item.vote
  if v0 == 0 and v1 == 0:
    mapped = cam_map[obs.cam].get(obs.dlc_id)
    if mapped is not None:
      item.mouse_id = mapped
      return

  # 3) otherwise remain unresolved by segmentation (likely ambiguous (1,1)):
  # use continuity (or leave None if you prefer)
  item.mouse_id = continuity_fallback_single(obs, b, prev_state, params)
```

And keep the mapping construction (B5) as-is.

If you also want **ambiguous segmentation (1,1)** to *not* trigger the DLC-group mapping (your message suggests that), the above does exactly that: DLC-group mapping is only used when segmentation is **empty** `(0,0)`, not when it’s ambiguous `(>0,>0)`.

## Parameters (suggested defaults)

```text
vote_thr = 0.01                 # your default
tau_swap = 4.0                  # commit swap if Δcost >= tau_swap (≈2σ in normalized units)
carry_swap_max_gap = 5 frames   # keep last known swap for short anchor dropouts

# Motion/continuity sigmas (mm) -> cost uses (d/sigma)^2
sigma_motion_anchor = 8.0
sigma_motion_other  = 15.0

# Anchor geometry sigmas (mm)
sigma_centroid = 60.0           # distance to mouse centroid
sigma_axis     = 35.0           # distance to head-tail axis

# Exclusive segmentation penalty (dimensionless, in cost units)
hard_exclusive = False          # if True: forbid contradictory assignment
penalty_excl   = 9.0            # strong discouragement (~3σ)
bonus_excl     = 0.5            # small reward for matching exclusives

# Weights (dimensionless) if you prefer explicit weights (optional)
w_cont  = 1.0
w_cent  = 1.0
w_axis  = 1.0
```

---

## `decide_swap_state(prev_state, anchors_now, params)`

**Goal:** pick `NOSWAP`, `SWAP`, or `UNKNOWN` per frame using anchors (e.g., head + tail_root).  
**Only geometry + continuity are primary.** Exclusive segmentation on anchors may be used as a *weak tie-breaker*.

### Inputs
- `prev_state.P_prev[p][m]`: previous 3D anchor position for anchor part `p` and mouse `m∈{0,1}` (may be None)
- `prev_state.P_prev2[p][m]`: optional second previous (for velocity prediction)
- `anchors_now[p]`: list of current 3D anchor items for part `p` (length 0..2), each has `.P` and `.exclusive` (0/1/None)

### Pseudocode
```text
function decide_swap_state(prev_state, anchors_now, params):

  # If we have a recently trusted swap_state and anchors are missing,
  # we can carry it forward for a short gap.
  if anchors_now provides no usable continuity info:
    if prev_state.swap_state_known_recently(within=params.carry_swap_max_gap):
      return prev_state.swap_state
    else:
      return UNKNOWN

  # Helper: predicted position (optional constant velocity)
  pred(p, m):
    P1 = prev_state.P_prev[p][m]
    P0 = prev_state.P_prev2[p][m]
    if P1 is None: return None
    if P0 is None: return P1
    return P1 + (P1 - P0)   # dt=1

  # Cost for a single anchor part under a hypothesis H
  # H in {NOSWAP, SWAP} means:
  #   NOSWAP: current mouse0 continues prev mouse0, current mouse1 continues prev mouse1
  #   SWAP:   current mouse0 continues prev mouse1, current mouse1 continues prev mouse0
  cost_part(p, H):
    curr = anchors_now[p]      # list of items with P
    if len(curr) == 0: return (0, 0)  # (cost, info_count)

    # choose targets depending on H
    # target0 = predicted position of the mouse0 track under H
    # target1 = predicted position of the mouse1 track under H
    if H == NOSWAP:
      T0 = pred(p, 0); T1 = pred(p, 1)
    else:  # SWAP
      T0 = pred(p, 1); T1 = pred(p, 0)

    if T0 is None or T1 is None:
      return (0, 0)

    sig = params.sigma_motion_anchor

    if len(curr) == 2:
      P1 = curr[0].P; P2 = curr[1].P

      # assign the two unlabeled points to (mouse0, mouse1) in the best way
      cA = (||P1-T0||/sig)^2 + (||P2-T1||/sig)^2
      cB = (||P1-T1||/sig)^2 + (||P2-T0||/sig)^2
      c  = min(cA, cB)

      # optional: weak exclusive segmentation tie-breaker on anchor items
      # Only applies if an anchor item has exclusive label and the chosen pairing contradicts it.
      c += exclusive_anchor_penalty_if_applicable(curr, H, T0, T1, params)

      return (c, 1)

    else:  # len(curr) == 1
      P = curr[0].P

      # With one point only, continuity alone can't distinguish SWAP/NOSWAP much.
      # Use the closer of the two targets; this contributes "some" evidence but weakly.
      c = min((||P-T0||/sig)^2, (||P-T1||/sig)^2)

      # If exclusive segmentation exists for this item, it can distinguish:
      # exclusive==0 means "this is mouse0 (true identity)".
      # Under hypothesis H, mouse0 corresponds to target T0.
      # If exclusive says mouse0, add cost against choosing T1, etc.
      c += exclusive_single_anchor_bias(curr[0], H, T0, T1, params)

      return (c, 1)

  # Sum costs over anchor parts
  C_no  = 0; I_no  = 0
  C_sw  = 0; I_sw  = 0
  for p in params.anchor_parts:
    (c, i) = cost_part(p, NOSWAP); C_no += c; I_no += i
    (c, i) = cost_part(p, SWAP);   C_sw += c; I_sw += i

  if min(I_no, I_sw) == 0:
    # no usable continuity info
    if prev_state.swap_state_known_recently(within=params.carry_swap_max_gap):
      return prev_state.swap_state
    return UNKNOWN

  # Decide with confidence margin
  if abs(C_no - C_sw) < params.tau_swap:
    # not confident; carry forward if recently stable
    if prev_state.swap_state_known_recently(within=params.carry_swap_max_gap):
      return prev_state.swap_state
    return UNKNOWN

  return NOSWAP if C_no < C_sw else SWAP
```

**Interpretation of `tau_swap`:** costs are normalized squared distances; `Δcost≈4` corresponds roughly to a 2σ preference if one anchor dominates.

---

## `assignment_cost(item, mouse_id, bodypart, mouse_model, prev_state, swap_state, params)`

This cost is used when segmentation is **not exclusive** (i.e., ambiguous `(1,1)` or absent `(0,0)`), to choose between mouse0 vs mouse1 based on continuity + anchor geometry.

### Mouse model fields (per mouse)
From your assigned anchors (after swap decision):
- `mouse_model[m].centroid` (e.g., midpoint of head and tail_root if both exist; else head alone; else prev)
- `mouse_model[m].axis_line` (point+direction from tail_root→head if both exist; else None)

### Pseudocode
```text
function assignment_cost(item, m, bodypart, mouse_model, prev_state, swap_state, params):

  if item.P is None:
    return +inf  # not used for singles; singles handled separately

  P = item.P
  cost = 0

  # (0) Exclusive segmentation: strong constraint if present
  if item.exclusive is not None:
    if item.exclusive == m:
      cost -= params.bonus_excl
    else:
      if params.hard_exclusive:
        return +inf
      cost += params.penalty_excl

  # (1) Temporal continuity for this bodypart
  # Prefer predicted position for this bodypart+mouse if available.
  P1 = prev_state.P_prev_bodypart[bodypart][m]   # may be None
  P0 = prev_state.P_prev2_bodypart[bodypart][m]  # may be None
  if P1 is not None:
    Ppred = P1 if P0 is None else (P1 + (P1 - P0))
    sig = params.sigma_motion_anchor if bodypart in params.anchor_parts else params.sigma_motion_other
    cost += params.w_cont * (||P - Ppred||/sig)^2

  # (2) Proximity to anchor-defined centroid
  if mouse_model[m].centroid is not None:
    sig = params.sigma_centroid
    cost += params.w_cent * (||P - mouse_model[m].centroid||/sig)^2

  # (3) Proximity to anchor-defined body axis
  if mouse_model[m].axis_line is not None:
    d = distance_point_to_line(P, mouse_model[m].axis_line)
    sig = params.sigma_axis
    cost += params.w_axis * (d/sig)^2

  return cost
```

### Practical notes
- If you find centroid/axis terms overpower continuity, increase `sigma_centroid`/`sigma_axis` (weakens them).
- If identity flips persist during occlusion, decrease `sigma_motion_*` (strengthens continuity).

---

## Missing anchors / missing previous state behavior (deterministic)
- If `decide_swap_state` returns `UNKNOWN` and there is a **recent** known swap state (≤ `carry_swap_max_gap`), **reuse it**.
- If no recent swap state exists, allow the bodypart assignment to be driven by:
  - continuity where available,
  - otherwise centroid/axis if can be built from whatever anchors exist,
  - otherwise leave items unassigned until later evidence (or keep previous identity if you want “sticky labels”).

The segmentation analysis should allow the fur color to then dominate the assignment to the mouse id (0 brown mouse, 1 blueish mouse). Then there remains an influence of the groups from DLC assigned to a mouse (independent of which mouse they belong to, they belong to the same mouse). 

All that should limit the number of required identity swaps when analyzing assignment over time frames.

Assistant: Below are the two helper functions, written so they respect your **exclusive-only** philosophy and keep segmentation’s (fur-color) influence **dominant for identity**, while remaining **weak / optional** in the *swap-decision* stage.

I’ll give them in a form that plugs directly into the earlier `decide_swap_state → cost_part(...)` logic.

## 1) Penalty/bonus primitive

```text
penalty_for_exclusive(exclusive_label, assigned_mouse_id,
                      penalty, bonus):
  # exclusive_label: 0|1|None   (None = ambiguous or no info)
  # assigned_mouse_id: 0|1
  if exclusive_label is None:
    return 0
  if exclusive_label == assigned_mouse_id:
    return -bonus      # small reward
  else:
    return +penalty    # small penalty
```

Recommended for **swap decision only** (weak):  
- `penalty_excl_swap = 0.5` to `2.0`  
- `bonus_excl_swap   = 0.1` to `0.5`  
Set both to 0 to disable entirely.

For the **final identity assignment cost** (strong), you already had bigger values like `penalty_excl ≈ 9`, which is fine; keep those separate parameters from swap-stage.

---

## 2) `exclusive_anchor_penalty_if_applicable(...)` for the 2-point anchor case

When an anchor part yields **two unlabeled 3D points** (say `P1`, `P2`), your continuity test evaluates two pairings:

- Pairing A: `P1 → mouse0`, `P2 → mouse1`
- Pairing B: `P1 → mouse1`, `P2 → mouse0`

This helper returns **two additive penalties** `(penA, penB)` so you can do:

- `cA_total = cA + penA`
- `cB_total = cB + penB`

```text
exclusive_anchor_pair_penalties(item1, item2, params):
  # item1.exclusive is 0|1|None, same for item2
  # Pairing A: item1->mouse0, item2->mouse1
  penA = penalty_for_exclusive(item1.exclusive, 0,
                               params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap) \
       + penalty_for_exclusive(item2.exclusive, 1,
                               params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap)

  # Pairing B: item1->mouse1, item2->mouse0
  penB = penalty_for_exclusive(item1.exclusive, 1,
                               params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap) \
       + penalty_for_exclusive(item2.exclusive, 0,
                               params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap)

  return (penA, penB)
```

### How to use inside your `cost_part(p, H)` (two-current-anchor-points)
Replace:

```text
cA = dist(P1,T0)^2 + dist(P2,T1)^2
cB = dist(P1,T1)^2 + dist(P2,T0)^2
c  = min(cA, cB)
c += exclusive_anchor_penalty_if_applicable(...)
```

with the cleaner:

```text
(penA, penB) = exclusive_anchor_pair_penalties(curr[0], curr[1], params)

cA = (||P1-T0||/sig)^2 + (||P2-T1||/sig)^2 + penA
cB = (||P1-T1||/sig)^2 + (||P2-T0||/sig)^2 + penB
c  = min(cA, cB)
```

This keeps the segmentation influence *only* as a weak bias in the swap decision.

---

## 3) `exclusive_single_anchor_bias(...)` for the 1-point anchor case

If an anchor part yields **one** 3D point `P`, continuity alone can’t distinguish `NOSWAP` vs `SWAP` reliably. But if segmentation is **exclusive**, you can bias which target (mouse0 vs mouse1) that point should be associated with for the purpose of computing the hypothesis cost.

Return `(pen0, pen1)` for associating this point with mouse0 vs mouse1:

```text
exclusive_single_anchor_option_penalties(item, params):
  pen0 = penalty_for_exclusive(item.exclusive, 0,
                               params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap)
  pen1 = penalty_for_exclusive(item.exclusive, 1,
                               params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap)
  return (pen0, pen1)
```

Then in the `len(curr)==1` case compute:

```text
(pen0, pen1) = exclusive_single_anchor_option_penalties(curr[0], params)

d0 = (||P - T0||/sig)^2 + pen0   # interpret as "this point is mouse0"
d1 = (||P - T1||/sig)^2 + pen1   # interpret as "this point is mouse1"

c  = min(d0, d1)
```

Again: if `exclusive` is `None` (ambiguous `(1,1)` or no signal), penalties are 0 and this reduces to pure continuity.

---

## Why this matches your intent
- If segmentation is **ambiguous** `(1,1)`, then `exclusive=None` ⇒ these helpers contribute **nothing**.
- If segmentation is **clear** (fur-color dominates), then `exclusive=0/1` ⇒ it can:
  - dominate final mouse assignment (your Stage B rules),
  - and *lightly* stabilize swap decision when continuity is weak (optional).

---

If you want, I can now fold these helpers back into the full `decide_swap_state` pseudocode so the whole function is self-contained and ready to implement verbatim.

User: Yes, please finish the pseudocode.

Assistant: Below is a **complete, self-contained pseudocode** for `decide_swap_state(...)` including the helper functions and the exact control flow. It is consistent with your design:

- Stage A has already ensured the 3D points are **geometrically non-contradictory**.
- Segmentation (fur color) should dominate **identity assignment**, but here in swap estimation it is only a **weak optional bias** and only when **exclusive**.
- Swap decision uses **anchors + temporal continuity**; if insufficient evidence, it yields `UNKNOWN` and/or carries forward the last stable state.

## Complete pseudocode: swap decision per frame

```text id="1w2znk"
enum SwapState { NOSWAP, SWAP, UNKNOWN }

# -------------------------
# Helpers: exclusive logic
# -------------------------
penalty_for_exclusive(exclusive_label, assigned_mouse_id, penalty, bonus):
  # exclusive_label: 0|1|None
  # assigned_mouse_id: 0|1
  if exclusive_label is None:
    return 0
  if exclusive_label == assigned_mouse_id:
    return -bonus
  else:
    return +penalty

exclusive_anchor_pair_penalties(item1, item2, params):
  # Pairing A: item1->mouse0, item2->mouse1
  penA = penalty_for_exclusive(item1.exclusive, 0, params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap) \
       + penalty_for_exclusive(item2.exclusive, 1, params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap)

  # Pairing B: item1->mouse1, item2->mouse0
  penB = penalty_for_exclusive(item1.exclusive, 1, params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap) \
       + penalty_for_exclusive(item2.exclusive, 0, params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap)

  return (penA, penB)

exclusive_single_anchor_option_penalties(item, params):
  pen0 = penalty_for_exclusive(item.exclusive, 0, params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap)
  pen1 = penalty_for_exclusive(item.exclusive, 1, params.penalty_excl_swap, params.bonus_excl_swap)
  return (pen0, pen1)


# ----------------------------------------
# Helpers: continuity prediction (optional)
# ----------------------------------------
predict(prev1, prev2):
  # constant velocity prediction if possible
  if prev1 is None:
    return None
  if prev2 is None:
    return prev1
  return prev1 + (prev1 - prev2)


# ----------------------------------------
# Main: decide_swap_state
# ----------------------------------------
decide_swap_state(prev_state, anchors_now, params):

  # anchors_now[p] is list of 0..2 anchor items for part p (each item has .P and .exclusive)
  # prev_state stores:
  #   prev_state.anchor_prev[p][m]  : 3D or None  (last frame)
  #   prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][m] : 3D or None  (frame before last)
  #   prev_state.swap_state         : last chosen swap state
  #   prev_state.swap_age           : frames since last confident swap decision

  # -----------------------------
  # Step 0: quick "can we decide?"
  # -----------------------------
  usable_parts = []  # anchor parts with any continuity reference for at least one mouse
  for p in params.anchor_parts:
    if len(anchors_now[p]) == 0:
      continue
    # need at least one previous anchor position to create targets
    if prev_state.anchor_prev[p][0] is not None or prev_state.anchor_prev[p][1] is not None:
      usable_parts.append(p)

  if len(usable_parts) == 0:
    # no continuity possible -> carry forward if recent, else unknown
    if prev_state.swap_age <= params.carry_swap_max_gap:
      return prev_state.swap_state
    return UNKNOWN

  # ------------------------------------------------
  # Step 1: define cost for one anchor part and one hypothesis
  # ------------------------------------------------
  # Hypothesis H means mapping of "current mouse tracks" to "previous mouse tracks"
  # NOSWAP: current mouse0 continues prev mouse0; mouse1 continues prev mouse1
  # SWAP  : current mouse0 continues prev mouse1; mouse1 continues prev mouse0

  cost_part(p, H):
    curr_list = anchors_now[p]  # 0..2 items
    if len(curr_list) == 0:
      return (0, 0)  # (cost, info_count)

    # Targets from previous frame under hypothesis H
    if H == NOSWAP:
      T0 = predict(prev_state.anchor_prev[p][0], prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][0])
      T1 = predict(prev_state.anchor_prev[p][1], prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][1])
    else:  # SWAP
      T0 = predict(prev_state.anchor_prev[p][1], prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][1])
      T1 = predict(prev_state.anchor_prev[p][0], prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][0])

    # If both missing, no information
    if T0 is None and T1 is None:
      return (0, 0)

    sig = params.sigma_motion_anchor

    if len(curr_list) == 2 and T0 is not None and T1 is not None:
      item1 = curr_list[0]; P1 = item1.P
      item2 = curr_list[1]; P2 = item2.P

      (penA, penB) = exclusive_anchor_pair_penalties(item1, item2, params)

      # Pairing A: item1->mouse0, item2->mouse1
      cA = (||P1 - T0||/sig)^2 + (||P2 - T1||/sig)^2 + penA

      # Pairing B: item1->mouse1, item2->mouse0
      cB = (||P1 - T1||/sig)^2 + (||P2 - T0||/sig)^2 + penB

      return (min(cA, cB), 1)

    # If only one target exists (one mouse missing previously), treat as single-target match
    if len(curr_list) == 2:
      # still can provide info, but only w.r.t. the available target
      # pick the point closer to the available target
      T = T0 if T1 is None else T1
      if T is None:
        return (0, 0)
      P1 = curr_list[0].P
      P2 = curr_list[1].P
      c = min((||P1 - T||/sig)^2, (||P2 - T||/sig)^2)
      # exclusive bias is not meaningful here (no identity opposition), keep it out
      return (c, 1)

    # len(curr_list) == 1
    item = curr_list[0]; P = item.P

    # If both targets exist, allow matching to either; exclusive (if any) biases that choice slightly.
    if T0 is not None and T1 is not None:
      (pen0, pen1) = exclusive_single_anchor_option_penalties(item, params)
      d0 = (||P - T0||/sig)^2 + pen0
      d1 = (||P - T1||/sig)^2 + pen1
      return (min(d0, d1), 1)

    # If only one target exists:
    T = T0 if T1 is None else T1
    if T is None:
      return (0, 0)
    c = (||P - T||/sig)^2
    # exclusive bias not meaningful without two targets
    return (c, 1)

  # ------------------------------------------------
  # Step 2: sum costs over anchor parts
  # ------------------------------------------------
  C_no = 0; I_no = 0
  C_sw = 0; I_sw = 0
  for p in params.anchor_parts:
    (c, i) = cost_part(p, NOSWAP); C_no += c; I_no += i
    (c, i) = cost_part(p, SWAP);   C_sw += c; I_sw += i

  # Require some minimal information count
  if min(I_no, I_sw) == 0:
    if prev_state.swap_age <= params.carry_swap_max_gap:
      return prev_state.swap_state
    return UNKNOWN

  # ------------------------------------------------
  # Step 3: confidence threshold (margin test)
  # ------------------------------------------------
  delta = abs(C_no - C_sw)

  if delta < params.tau_swap:
    # not confident enough; carry forward if recently stable
    if prev_state.swap_age <= params.carry_swap_max_gap:
      return prev_state.swap_state
    return UNKNOWN

  return NOSWAP if C_no < C_sw else SWAP
```

---

## Recommended “swap-stage” parameter values
These are deliberately **weak** so fur-color segmentation dominates later, but swap estimation doesn’t thrash:

```text
sigma_motion_anchor = 8.0 mm
tau_swap            = 4.0     # commit only if clear
carry_swap_max_gap  = 5 frames

penalty_excl_swap   = 1.0     # weak bias only
bonus_excl_swap     = 0.25
```

Set `penalty_excl_swap=bonus_excl_swap=0` to disable segmentation influence in swap decision entirely.

---

## How to update `prev_state` after decision
Deterministic update rule:

```text
if swap_state is NOSWAP or SWAP:
  prev_state.swap_state = swap_state
  prev_state.swap_age   = 0
else:
  prev_state.swap_age  += 1
```

And store assigned anchor positions (once Stage B assigns identities to anchor points) into:
- `anchor_prev2 <- anchor_prev`
- `anchor_prev <- current_assigned`

---

If you want the final piece fully pinned down too, I can write the complementary function `build_mouse_models(...)` (centroid + axis from anchors, with fallback to previous frame) in the same self-contained style.

User: Yes, please do so. And have a look to finally code everything.

Assistant: Below is a **complete `build_mouse_models(...)` pseudocode**, designed to be dropped into the Stage B pipeline you now have:

- It **uses the already-decided `swap_state`** (NOSWAP/SWAP/UNKNOWN).
- It **assigns current anchor 3D points to mouse0/mouse1** using continuity targets (and optional weak exclusive bias).
- It then builds per-mouse **centroid** + **axis line** (tail_root → head) with sane fallbacks.
- It returns both the **models** and the **assigned anchor positions** so you can update `prev_state`.

---

## `build_mouse_models(...)` — self-contained pseudocode

```text
function build_mouse_models(prev_state, anchors_now, swap_state, params):

  # anchors_now[p] : list of 0..2 items (each item has .P and .exclusive)
  # params.anchor_parts includes at least ["head","tail_root"]
  # prev_state stores:
  #   prev_state.anchor_prev[p][m], prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][m]
  #   prev_state.centroid_prev[m] (optional)
  #   prev_state.axis_prev[m]     (optional line: point+dir)
  #
  # Output:
  #   mouse_model[m] with fields {centroid, axis_line, head, tail_root, valid_axis}
  #   anchor_assigned[p][m] : 3D or None

  # ----------------------------
  # helpers
  # ----------------------------
  predict(prev1, prev2):
    if prev1 is None: return None
    if prev2 is None: return prev1
    return prev1 + (prev1 - prev2)     # constant velocity

  # weak exclusive penalties (swap-stage)
  penalty_for_exclusive(exclusive_label, assigned_mouse_id):
    if exclusive_label is None: return 0
    if exclusive_label == assigned_mouse_id: return -params.bonus_excl_swap
    return +params.penalty_excl_swap

  # choose best assignment of two current points to (mouse0,mouse1)
  best_pairing_cost(P1, P2, T0, T1, item1, item2, sig):
    # pairing A: P1->0, P2->1
    cA = (||P1-T0||/sig)^2 + (||P2-T1||/sig)^2 \
       + penalty_for_exclusive(item1.exclusive, 0) \
       + penalty_for_exclusive(item2.exclusive, 1)

    # pairing B: P1->1, P2->0
    cB = (||P1-T1||/sig)^2 + (||P2-T0||/sig)^2 \
       + penalty_for_exclusive(item1.exclusive, 1) \
       + penalty_for_exclusive(item2.exclusive, 0)

    if cA <= cB:
      return ("A", cA)   # A means item1->0 item2->1
    else:
      return ("B", cB)   # B means item1->1 item2->0

  # ----------------------------
  # Step 1: assign anchor points to mice using continuity targets
  # ----------------------------
  anchor_assigned = dict()  # anchor_assigned[p][m] = 3D or None
  for p in params.anchor_parts:
    anchor_assigned[p] = {0: None, 1: None}

    curr = anchors_now[p]        # 0..2 items
    if len(curr) == 0:
      continue

    # targets under swap_state
    # if UNKNOWN, we still compute both and use whichever yields a clear best (else remain partial)
    def targets_for(state):
      if state == NOSWAP:
        T0 = predict(prev_state.anchor_prev[p][0], prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][0])
        T1 = predict(prev_state.anchor_prev[p][1], prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][1])
      else:  # SWAP
        T0 = predict(prev_state.anchor_prev[p][1], prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][1])
        T1 = predict(prev_state.anchor_prev[p][0], prev_state.anchor_prev2[p][0])
      return (T0, T1)

    sig = params.sigma_motion_anchor

    if swap_state != UNKNOWN:
      (T0, T1) = targets_for(swap_state)

      if len(curr) == 2 and T0 is not None and T1 is not None:
        item1, item2 = curr[0], curr[1]
        P1, P2 = item1.P, item2.P
        (which, _) = best_pairing_cost(P1, P2, T0, T1, item1, item2, sig)
        if which == "A":
          anchor_assigned[p][0] = P1
          anchor_assigned[p][1] = P2
        else:
          anchor_assigned[p][0] = P2
          anchor_assigned[p][1] = P1

      elif len(curr) == 1:
        item = curr[0]; P = item.P
        # if only one point, assign it to nearest target if both exist
        if T0 is not None and T1 is not None:
          d0 = (||P-T0||/sig)^2 + penalty_for_exclusive(item.exclusive, 0)
          d1 = (||P-T1||/sig)^2 + penalty_for_exclusive(item.exclusive, 1)
          anchor_assigned[p][0] = P if d0 <= d1 else None
          anchor_assigned[p][1] = P if d1 <  d0 else None
        else:
          # only one target exists -> assign to that one
          if T0 is not None: anchor_assigned[p][0] = P
          if T1 is not None: anchor_assigned[p][1] = P

      else:
        # len(curr)==2 but missing targets: partial assignment possible
        # if only one target exists, assign closest point to that target
        item1, item2 = curr[0], curr[1]
        P1, P2 = item1.P, item2.P
        if (T0 is not None) and (T1 is None):
          anchor_assigned[p][0] = P1 if ||P1-T0|| <= ||P2-T0|| else P2
        if (T1 is not None) and (T0 is None):
          anchor_assigned[p][1] = P1 if ||P1-T1|| <= ||P2-T1|| else P2

    else:
      # swap_state UNKNOWN:
      # try NOSWAP and SWAP; if one yields clearly smaller total cost, use it; else do minimal/partial assignment
      (T0n, T1n) = targets_for(NOSWAP)
      (T0s, T1s) = targets_for(SWAP)

      # score both states using available targets; if insufficient info, fall back to exclusives or leave None
      def score_state(T0, T1):
        if len(curr)==2 and T0 is not None and T1 is not None:
          item1,item2 = curr[0],curr[1]
          P1,P2 = item1.P,item2.P
          (_, c) = best_pairing_cost(P1,P2,T0,T1,item1,item2,sig)
          return c
        if len(curr)==1 and T0 is not None and T1 is not None:
          item=curr[0]; P=item.P
          d0=(||P-T0||/sig)^2; d1=(||P-T1||/sig)^2
          return min(d0,d1)
        return +inf

      Cn = score_state(T0n,T1n)
      Cs = score_state(T0s,T1s)

      if min(Cn, Cs) < +inf and abs(Cn - Cs) >= params.tau_swap:
        chosen_state = NOSWAP if Cn < Cs else SWAP
        # re-run assignment under chosen_state (same logic as above)
        # (implementation: call build_mouse_models again with swap_state=chosen_state,
        #  or duplicate the small assignment block)
        swap_state = chosen_state
        # For pseudocode brevity: assume we now assign with the non-UNKNOWN block.
        return build_mouse_models(prev_state, anchors_now, swap_state, params)

      # else: remain conservative: use exclusive-only if it separates, otherwise leave unassigned
      if len(curr)==1 and curr[0].exclusive is not None:
        anchor_assigned[p][curr[0].exclusive] = curr[0].P
      if len(curr)==2:
        # if they are exclusively 0 and 1, assign accordingly
        e1,e2 = curr[0].exclusive, curr[1].exclusive
        if e1 in {0,1} and e2 in {0,1} and e1 != e2:
          anchor_assigned[p][e1] = curr[0].P
          anchor_assigned[p][e2] = curr[1].P

  # ----------------------------
  # Step 2: build per-mouse centroid + axis line using assigned anchors with fallbacks
  # ----------------------------
  mouse_model = dict()
  eps_axis = 1e-6  # mm

  for m in [0,1]:
    head = anchor_assigned.get("head", {}).get(m)
    tail = anchor_assigned.get("tail_root", {}).get(m)

    # fallback to previous anchors if current missing
    if head is None:
      head = prev_state.anchor_prev["head"][m]
    if tail is None:
      tail = prev_state.anchor_prev["tail_root"][m]

    # centroid
    if head is not None and tail is not None:
      centroid = 0.5*(head + tail)
    elif head is not None:
      centroid = head
    elif tail is not None:
      centroid = tail
    else:
      centroid = prev_state.centroid_prev.get(m)  # may be None

    # axis line: prefer current head+tail; else reuse previous axis if available
    axis_line = None
    valid_axis = False
    if head is not None and tail is not None:
      d = head - tail
      if ||d|| > eps_axis:
        axis_line = (tail, d/||d||)   # point+unit_dir
        valid_axis = True
    if axis_line is None:
      # fallback: previous axis if you stored it
      axis_line = prev_state.axis_prev.get(m)  # may be None
      valid_axis = (axis_line is not None)

    mouse_model[m] = {
      "centroid": centroid,
      "axis_line": axis_line,
      "head": head,
      "tail_root": tail,
      "valid_axis": valid_axis
    }

  return mouse_model, anchor_assigned, swap_state
```

### Why this is stable
- If swap_state is confident, assignment is purely continuity-driven (with optional weak exclusive bias).
- If swap_state is UNKNOWN, it *tries* to disambiguate; otherwise it stays conservative and uses exclusives only when they truly separate.

# “Have a look to finally code everything” — concrete coding plan (based on your files)

I checked your data formats:

- `cameras.json` contains **K** (fx,fy,cx,cy), **R,t** (world→cam), and camera names `cam1_top`, `cam2_front`, `cam3_side`. Camera center matches `-Rᵀ t` (consistent).  
- `dlc_long.csv` is already in the ideal long format: `frame, camera, individual(mouse0/mouse1), bodypart, x, y, likelihood` with 1800 frames and 10 bodyparts.

### Minimal repo structure (practical)
- `frontend.py`  
  - load cameras.json into Camera objects (project + ray)  
  - load dlc_long.csv into dense arrays `[T,C,I,B,(x,y,lik)]`
- `geometry.py`  
  - ray building, ray-angle gate, closest-approach, bbox gate, fast reproj gate, epipolar gate (optional)
  - hypothesis enumeration + disjoint brute-force selection
- `point_ba.py`  
  - wrapper for `ceres_point_ba.solve_point(...)` (or SciPy fallback)
- `identity.py`  
  - segmentation vote extraction (your Gaussian window)  
  - `decide_swap_state`, `build_mouse_models`, `assignment_cost`, singles logic
- `pipeline.py`  
  - processes frames, updates `prev_state`, writes outputs (cleaned 2D assignments + 3D points)

### Ceres module: simplest clean way
Given your current extension is complex and doesn’t expose a point-only solver cleanly, the cleanest is:

- Add a **second** pybind module, e.g. `ceres_point_ba`, whose only job is:
  - input: one initial 3D point + N observations (cam index, u,v, optional weight)
  - output: refined 3D point + residual stats

CMake change (conceptually):
```cmake
pybind11_add_module(ceres_point_ba src/ceres_point_ba_module.cpp)
target_link_libraries(ceres_point_ba PRIVATE Eigen3::Eigen Ceres::ceres)
```

This avoids entangling with the existing `mouse_ba` design.

If you prefer **one** module, we can instead add a `solve_point(...)` function into your existing `mouse_ba_module.cpp`, but the separate module is cleaner and easier to debug.
