### What I changed / added

- New file: **`src/ceres_point_ba_module.cpp`**  
  Implements `ceres_point_ba.solve_point(...)`:
  - optimizes **one 3D point** \(P\) in world coordinates
  - minimizes reprojection error over N observations (2–3 rays typical)
  - **undistorted pinhole** model: \(P_c = R P_w + t\), \(u=fx x/z+cx\), \(v=fy y/z+cy\)
  - optional robust loss: `none|huber|cauchy|soft_l1|arctan`
  - optional per-observation `sigmas` (else uses `sigma_pix`)
  - returns refined point + residual stats

- Updated **`CMakeLists.txt`**  
  Builds `ceres_point_ba` from `src/ceres_point_ba_module.cpp`.  
  Keeps the old `mouse_ba` target **only if** `src/mouse_ba_module.cpp` exists (it currently does not, so it won’t build it).

    P_init,          # (3,)
    cam_idx,         # (N,) int camera indices
    uv,              # (N,2) observed pixels
    cameras,         # dict with fx,fy,cx,cy (C,), R (C,3,3), t (C,3)
    sigmas=None,     # (N,) optional per obs sigma
    sigma_pix=1.0,
    max_num_iterations=50,

    verbose=False,
)

Assistant: Yes — I built that in, but it’s **off by default** so it won’t spam runs.

### Where the debug output is
There are two layers:

1) **Per-hypothesis diagnostics (Stage A)**  
   In `mice3d/stage_a.py`, every tested hypothesis can record:
   - which **gate** it failed (epi / angle / closest-approach / bbox / fast-reproj)
   - initial guess `P_init`
   - BA stats (RMS, max, per-view residuals) for accepted ones  
   This is written into an in-memory `debug_log` structure.

2) **Per-frame summary + CSV export**
   In `mice3d/pipeline.py`, if enabled, it writes:
   - `out/<run>_debug_frame_<frame>.json` (or one consolidated `*_debug.json`, depending on flag)
   - counts of: triplets tested/accepted, pairs tested/accepted, singles, etc.

### How to enable it
Run with:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... --debug --debug-save
```

- `--debug` turns on collection + console summaries
- `--debug-save` writes the JSON files

(If you only want the JSON without console prints, use `--debug-save` alone.)

### What you’ll see in the debug files
For each `(frame, bodypart)`:
- candidate count: triplets/pairs
- selected hypothesis (obs IDs)
- gate failures histogram
- BA metrics for each accepted hypothesis:
  - `rms_px`, `max_px`, `chi2`, `residuals_by_cam`

If you want the log to also include *which exact DLC rows* (frame/cam/individual/bodypart) a hypothesis came from, I can add the source row index to each `Obs` and dump it too.

RuntimeError: ceres_point_ba module not available. Build the extension via ./build.sh

Assistant: That error is just **Python import path**, not a build failure.

Your `build.sh` copies the compiled module to the **project root**:

```
dlc_mouse_cleaning/ceres_point_ba.cpython-311-x86_64-linux-gnu.so
```

…but you’re running from `dlc_mouse_cleaning/python/`, and `..` (the repo root) is **not** on `sys.path`, so `import ceres_point_ba` can’t see it.

## Quick fix (no code changes)

From your `python/` folder, first verify the `.so` is really one directory up:

```bash
cd ~/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/dlc_mouse_cleaning/python
ls -1 ../ceres_point_ba*.so
```

If you see it, run with `PYTHONPATH` including the repo root:

```bash
export PYTHONPATH="$(pwd):$(pwd)/..:$PYTHONPATH"
python run_mouse3d.py --cameras ... --dlc ... --seg-dir ... --out ...
```

That’s enough.

### Alternative: run from repo root (cleanest)
```bash
cd ~/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/dlc_mouse_cleaning
PYTHONPATH=python:. python python/run_mouse3d.py --cameras ... --dlc ... --seg-dir ... --out ...
```

- `python` (folder) → lets it import `mice3d`
- `.` (repo root) → lets it import `ceres_point_ba`

## Permanent fix (recommended): make the runner add both paths automatically

Edit the **top of** `python/run_mouse3d.py` (before importing `mice3d`):

```python
import os, sys
THIS_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))      # .../python
REPO_ROOT = os.path.abspath(os.path.join(THIS_DIR, ".."))  # repo root

for p in (THIS_DIR, REPO_ROOT):
    if p not in sys.path:
        sys.path.insert(0, p)
```

Then you can run it without any `PYTHONPATH` exports.

---

## If `ls ../ceres_point_ba*.so` shows “No such file”
Then you’re likely **building in a different checkout** than the one you’re executing (your traceback shows `/media/...` paths while your build log shows `/home/...`). In that case:

- rebuild from the *same* tree you run from, or
- just copy the `.so` into the `python/` folder you’re running in:

```bash
cp -f /path/to/dlc_mouse_cleaning/ceres_point_ba*.so ~/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/dlc_mouse_cleaning/python/
```

(Replace `/path/to/...` with the location that actually contains the `.so`.)

If you paste the output of `ls -la .. | head` from inside `python/`, I can tell immediately whether you’re in a different clone/mount and which path to use.

Assistant: You’ve got **three separate issues** mixed together:

1) `--debug/--debug-save` didn’t exist in your runner (so argparse rejects them)  
2) the `from __future__` placement (you fixed that correctly in your current file) fileciteturn2file0  
3) the **segmentation fault** (likely in a native library: either `ceres_point_ba` or OpenCV mask reading)

I fixed (1) and also made it easier to diagnose (3).

---

## 1) Updated runner + debug flags (and faulthandler)
Your current `run_mouse3d.py` has **no debug args**, so `--debug --debug-save` will always error. fileciteturn2file0

I produced an updated `run_mouse3d.py` that adds:

- `--debug` (prints per-frame summary)
- `--debug-save` (writes `*_debug.jsonl`)
- `--faulthandler` (prints Python stack on segfault)
- `--seg-backend imageio|opencv` (default **imageio** to avoid OpenCV crashes)
- `--verbose-ceres` and `--trace-ceres` (deep diagnostics)

Download and overwrite your current file:

- [Updated run_mouse3d.py](sandbox:/mnt/data/run_mouse3d.py)

---

## 2) Updated segmentation reader (to avoid OpenCV segfaults)
Because you run with `--seg-dir`, your pipeline reads thousands of PNGs. Your current implementation uses OpenCV (`cv2.imread`) which *can* segfault on some setups. I changed it so **default backend is `imageio`** (still can switch back to OpenCV if wanted).

Download and overwrite the `mice3d/` package:

- [Updated mice3d.zip](sandbox:/mnt/data/mice3d.zip)

Unzip into your `python/` folder so you have:

```
python/
  run_mouse3d.py
  mice3d/
    segmentation.py
    ...
```

No rebuild is needed for these Python-only changes.

---

## 3) How to run now (with crash diagnostics)
From your `python/` directory:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py \
  --cameras ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2/cameras.json \
  --dlc ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_long.csv \
  --seg-dir ../../mouse_seg/preds/out2m_2 \
  --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run1 \
  --frames 0 5 \
  --debug --debug-save --faulthandler \
  --seg-backend imageio
```

This will:
- process only frames 0–4 (fast isolation),
- print per-frame summaries,
- write `../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run1_debug.jsonl`,
- and if it segfaults, you should get a Python-side crash stack instead of “core dumped”.

---

## 4) If it still segfaults: isolate whether it’s Ceres or segmentation
Run once **without segmentation**:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py \
  --cameras ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2/cameras.json \
  --dlc ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_long.csv \
  --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run1_noseg \
  --frames 0 5 \
  --debug --faulthandler
```

- If the segfault disappears → it was almost certainly OpenCV/video/mask I/O.
- If it still segfaults → it’s likely inside `ceres_point_ba`.

For the Ceres case, add:

```bash
--trace-ceres --verbose-ceres
```

so the last printed “TRACE ceres_point_ba …” line tells you exactly which solve input triggers it.

---

## 5) Your `cameras.json` looks fine for the solver
Nothing stands out as incompatible with the assumptions (undistorted pinhole, world→cam extrinsics Pc = R Pw + t). Your file includes the expected fields and consistent camera definitions. fileciteturn1file0

Segmentation fault (core dumped)
(mouseba) hellwich@Artemis:~/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/dlc_mouse_cleaning/python$

Assistant: Good — your crash trace localizes the segfault *inside* `_solve_point_ba` right after (or during teardown of) `ceres_point_ba.solve_point(...)`. That strongly points to a **C++ lifetime/ownership bug**, not your camera file or segmentation.

### Root cause (what was wrong)
In the first version of `ceres_point_ba_module.cpp`, we:

1) **Reused one `LossFunction*`** across multiple residual blocks, and  
2) Did not explicitly control **Ceres ownership** of that pointer, and  
3) The `loss_fn` lifetime was not guaranteed to outlive the `ceres::Problem` destructor.

Depending on Ceres defaults, this can lead to **double-free / use-after-free** when the `Problem` is destroyed — which matches “solver runs, prints iterations, then segfaults”.

### Fix applied
I patched the C++ module to make it safe by:

- Explicitly setting:  
  `problem_options.loss_function_ownership = ceres::DO_NOT_TAKE_OWNERSHIP`
- Ensuring `loss_fn` **outlives** `ceres::Problem` by creating it **before** the `Problem` object (so it gets destroyed after).

---

## ✅ Download the patched C++ file
Replace your repo’s `src/ceres_point_ba_module.cpp` with this:

- [Patched src/ceres_point_ba_module.cpp](sandbox:/mnt/data/src/ceres_point_ba_module.cpp)

Assistant: Yes — we can make this *much* more flexible without making it brittle.

I updated the **segmentation directory reader** so it **auto-detects** layouts like yours:

- subdirs: `top/`, `front/`, `side/`
- filenames: `mask_000001.png`, `mask_000002.png`, …

It does this by:
1) mapping camera names like `cam1_top` → `top` (using suffix matching; `cam2_front` → `front`, etc.) based on your `cameras.json` camera names fileciteturn1file0  
2) inferring the filename pattern `<prefix>_<digits>.<ext>` from the directory (so it picks `mask`, padding `6`, and start index `1` automatically)

And I also added **optional overrides** in the runner in case auto-detection ever picks the wrong thing.

## 1) Scale up frames gradually (recommended ramp)
Instead of jumping to all frames immediately, grow in steps so you can spot parameter issues early:

```bash
# 1) 0..50
python run_mouse3d.py ... --frames 0 50

# 2) 0..200
python run_mouse3d.py ... --frames 0 200

# 3) all frames (omit --frames)
python run_mouse3d.py ... 
```

This helps because any remaining problems (rare ray degeneracy, missing masks, weird DLC values) often appear only occasionally.

---

## 2) Turn on debugging properly

### A) Console summary per frame
Your `Mouse3DReconstructor` prints a compact summary when `debug=True`, including mean RMS and swap state. fileciteturn3file0L107-L128

So: run with `--debug` once your runner supports it, or (quick hack) instantiate `Mouse3DReconstructor(..., debug=True)`.

**If your current runner doesn’t expose `--debug`:**
Add these args to `run_mouse3d.py`:

```python
p.add_argument("--debug", action="store_true")
p.add_argument("--debug-save", help="Write per-frame JSONL debug log to this path")
```

and pass them here:

```python
recon = Mouse3DReconstructor(
    rig=rig, dlc=dlc, seg_source=seg_source, params=params,
    debug=args.debug,
    debug_save_path=args.debug_save
)
```

That wires into the already-implemented `_debug_frame()`.

### B) Save detailed per-frame JSONL
This is the most useful debugging output because it records, per bodypart and item:

- `kind` (triplet/pair/single), `mouse_id`
- 3D point, BA stats (rms, max, chi2, num_obs)
- segmentation weights + votes for each observation

All already implemented in `_debug_frame`. fileciteturn3file0L130-L189

Run example (once the runner exposes it):

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... --frames 0 200 \
  --debug \
  --debug-save ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run1_debug.jsonl
```

---

## 3) What to look at first in the outputs

### A) `*_triangulated3d.csv`
Do these sanity checks:

- **How many 3D points per frame per bodypart?**  
  Expect 0–2; persistent 0 means gates too strict or missing camera data.
- **rms_px distribution:**  
  If lots of values near your acceptance threshold, tighten/loosen parameters.

Quick check:

```bash
python - <<'PY'
import pandas as pd
df = pd.read_csv("../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run1_triangulated3d.csv")
print(df["rms_px"].describe())
print("rows:", len(df))
print("by kind:", df["kind"].value_counts())
PY
```

### B) `*_dlc_assignments.csv`
Key columns:
- `new_mouse_id` (your cleaned assignment)
- `seg_w_m0`, `seg_w_m1`, `vote0`, `vote1`, `item_kind`

Check how often segmentation is decisive vs ambiguous:
```bash
python - <<'PY'
import pandas as pd
df = pd.read_csv("../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run1_dlc_assignments.csv")
# exclusive segmentation at obs level:
excl0 = (df["vote0"]==1) & (df["vote1"]==0)
excl1 = (df["vote1"]==1) & (df["vote0"]==0)
ambi  = (df["vote0"]==1) & (df["vote1"]==1)
none  = (df["vote0"]==0) & (df["vote1"]==0)
print("exclusive0", excl0.mean(), "exclusive1", excl1.mean(), "ambi", ambi.mean(), "none", none.mean())
print(df["item_kind"].value_counts())
PY
```

If `none` is high, increase seg radius / sigma or lower `vote_thr`.

---

## 4) Recommended parameter tuning sequence

### Step 1: stabilize geometry first (Stage A)
Tune only these first:
- `--accept-rms` and `--accept-rms-pair` (px)
- `--d-max` (mm)
- `--theta-trip`, `--theta-pair` (deg)
- `--e-init` (px)

Typical signs:
- too strict → many singles, few triplets/pairs
- too loose → wrong ray associations sneak in; RMS rises; identity gets harder

### Step 2: then tune segmentation voting (Stage B)
- `--seg-radius`, `--seg-sigma`, `--vote-thr`
- Your default `vote_thr=0.01` is fine if weights are normalized to sum to 1.

If you see fur-color dominating wrongly on extremal tips, increase radius slightly (captures more surrounding mask context), and keep your “vote for both if both > thr” behavior.

---

## 5) Identity-swap debugging over time
Once you run more frames (say 0–500), you can quantify swaps:

- For anchor parts (head, tail_root), count how often `mouse_id` flips between adjacent frames.
- In the debug JSONL you also log `swap_state` each frame. fileciteturn3file0L130-L138

If swap frequency is still high:
- strengthen temporal continuity in Stage B (in `assignment_cost` terms)
- consider increasing `tau_swap` so swap_state changes only when strongly supported.

ValueError: The truth value of an array with more than one element is ambiguous. Use a.any() or a.all()

Assistant: You’re past the hard parts now — this is a clean, deterministic bug in **Stage B state update**.

## 1) Why it crashed
This line (and a couple like it) uses Python’s `or` with a NumPy array:

```python
anchor_assigned.get(p, {}).get(0) or new_state.prev.get(p, {}).get(0)
```

But a NumPy array can’t be used as a boolean (“truth value … is ambiguous”), hence the exception.

## 2) Fix (patch `mice3d/stage_b.py`)
Find the block around the reported line (~553) and replace any `A or B` where `A` can be a NumPy array with an explicit `None` check.

### Minimal safe helper
Add near the top of `stage_b.py`:

```python
def _coalesce(a, b):
    return a if a is not None else b
```

### Then replace the failing lines
Change:

```python
new_state.anchor_prev[p][0] = anchor_assigned.get(p, {}).get(0) or new_state.prev.get(p, {}).get(0)
new_state.anchor_prev[p][1] = anchor_assigned.get(p, {}).get(1) or new_state.prev.get(p, {}).get(1)
```

to:

```python
new_state.anchor_prev[p][0] = _coalesce(anchor_assigned.get(p, {}).get(0), new_state.prev.get(p, {}).get(0))
new_state.anchor_prev[p][1] = _coalesce(anchor_assigned.get(p, {}).get(1), new_state.prev.get(p, {}).get(1))
```

Then **grep for other ` or ` uses** in `stage_b.py` and patch the same way:

```bash
grep -n " or " mice3d/stage_b.py
```

Any time the left-hand side might be a NumPy array, use `_coalesce(...)`.

After this edit, rerun from where it crashed (you can start a bit earlier, e.g. 950–1100):

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... --frames 950 1100 --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run1_part2 --debug
```

(Your current implementation resets state per run, so for continuity you’ll ultimately want one full run, but this is fine for debugging.)

---

## 3) Why `swap=UNKNOWN` all the time
That almost certainly means your **anchor bodypart names** configured in Stage B don’t match the actual DLC bodypart names (so the swap logic never finds anchors).

Quickly print your bodypart names:

```bash
python - <<'PY'
from mice3d.cameras import load_cameras_json
from mice3d.dlc import load_dlc_long_csv

rig = load_cameras_json("../../mouse_sim/out2m_2/cameras.json")
dlc = load_dlc_long_csv("../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_long.csv",
                        camera_order=[c.name for c in rig.cameras])
print("Bodyparts:", dlc.index.bodyparts)
PY
```

Then set anchors to two stable ones that actually exist (e.g. `nose` + `tail_base` / `tail_root`).

If your `run_mouse3d.py` doesn’t expose this as a CLI flag yet, do it directly in the runner:

```python
params.stage_b.anchor_parts = ["<YOUR_NOSE_NAME>", "<YOUR_TAILROOT_NAME>"]
```

Once anchors exist, you should start seeing `swap=NOSWAP` or `swap=SWAP` sometimes (not always, but not “UNKNOWN” forever).

Assistant: Great — you now have an end-to-end run that finishes and writes both CSVs. At this point the two things to focus on are:

1) **Why so many frames have `3D=0`** (Stage A is rejecting almost all pair/triplet hypotheses), and  
2) **Why `swap=UNKNOWN` forever** (Stage B never gets enough *anchor* 3D continuity to lock swap/no-swap).

Your bodypart list confirms the default anchor names are correct (`head`, `tail_root`). So the remaining issue is simply that **those anchors rarely get triangulated**, so Stage B can’t bootstrap continuity.

---

## A. Get more 3D points (Stage A tuning)
In `stage_a.py`, a hypothesis must pass several *pre-BA* gates before Ceres is even run: ray-angle, closest-approach distance, cage bbox, and fast reprojection (`e_init_px`). Those gates are currently the main suspects. (Once Ceres runs, your RMS values look good, so Ceres itself is fine.)

The fastest way forward is a **parameter sweep** that relaxes the two most “unnecessarily strict” gates first:

- **`--d-max`** (closest-approach in mm): raise from `20` → `80` (or even `120`)
- **`--e-init`** (fast reprojection gate in px): raise from `12` → `40` or `60`
- **`--theta-trip` / `--theta-pair`**: lower a bit (e.g. 0.6 / 0.4 deg)

Try this on a short window first:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py \
  --cameras ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2/cameras.json \
  --dlc ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_long.csv \
  --seg-dir ../../mouse_seg/preds/out2m_2 \
  --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/tuneA \
  --frames 0 200 \
  --d-max 80 \
  --e-init 50 \
  --theta-trip 0.6 \
  --theta-pair 0.4 \
  --debug
```

What you want to see: `3D=` increasing substantially (even if mean RMS stays ~0.3–0.6 px). If RMS stays low, relaxing those gates is “free”.

If `3D` still stays near zero: the **bbox gate** is likely rejecting most initial points. Your runner currently doesn’t expose `bbox_margin_mm`, but it exists in StageAParams. The quickest test is to temporarily set it in `run_mouse3d.py`:

```python
params.stage_a.bbox_margin_mm = 200.0  # was 20.0
```

(That’s a diagnostic knob; once you see improvement you can tighten again.)

---

## B. Why `swap=UNKNOWN` never resolves
In your pipeline’s debug print, `swap` comes from `PrevState.swap_state`. The swap decision needs **anchor 3D points across frames** (head/tail_root) to be confident. If Stage A rarely triangulates anchors, swap can’t bootstrap, and it will remain UNKNOWN.

So the sequence is:

1) Make Stage A triangulate `head` and `tail_root` in many consecutive frames (Section A).
2) Then you should start seeing `swap=NOSWAP` / `swap=SWAP` occasionally and later more consistently.

---

## C. Add “debug-save” (JSONL) so you can inspect *which bodyparts* triangulate
Your `Mouse3DReconstructor` already supports `debug_save_path` and writes a per-frame JSON line with *per-bodypart items, P, stats, votes, obs*, etc. fileciteturn6file0

If your current `run_mouse3d.py` doesn’t already expose it, add:

```python
p.add_argument("--debug-save", default=None, help="Write per-frame debug JSONL to this file")
```

and pass it into the reconstructor:

```python
recon = Mouse3DReconstructor(
    rig=rig, dlc=dlc, seg_source=seg_source, params=params,
    debug=args.debug,
    debug_save_path=args.debug_save
)
```

Then run:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... \
  --frames 0 500 \
  --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run_debug \
  --debug \
  --debug-save ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run_debug.jsonl
```

### Quick analysis of the debug JSONL
Example: “How often do anchors get 3D points?”

```bash
python - <<'PY'
import json
from collections import Counter

path = "../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run_debug.jsonl"
cnt = Counter()
n = 0
with open(path, "r") as f:
    for line in f:
        n += 1
        rec = json.loads(line)
        for bp in ("head", "tail_root"):
            has3d = any(it.get("P") is not None for it in rec["bodyparts"].get(bp, []))
            if has3d:
                cnt[bp] += 1
print("frames:", n)
print("anchor 3D frames:", dict(cnt))
PY
```

If `head`/`tail_root` show up rarely, focus Stage A tuning until they show up frequently.

---

## D. Sanity-check the output CSVs
Remember: `*_triangulated3d.csv` only contains rows where `item.P` **and** `item.mouse_id` exist. fileciteturn6file0  
So it can under-report raw triangulation attempts. For raw geometry success, your per-frame `3D=` counter is better, and the debug JSONL is best.

The `python - <<'PY' ... PY` heredoc must be run in the **shell**, not inside the Python REPL (that’s why you saw `SyntaxError` earlier). You did the right thing afterwards by running the imports directly.

(mouseba) hellwich@Artemis:~/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/dlc_mouse_cleaning/python

In my run_mouse3d.py there is no params.stage_a.bbox_margin_mm

Assistant: Good news first: your “tuneA” run shows **exactly the same 3D yield pattern** as before, so the gates you relaxed (`d-max`, `e-init`, `theta-*`) were **not the bottleneck** in those frames. The bottleneck is almost certainly:

- **bbox gate** (`bbox_margin_mm`, default 20 mm), or
- **simply not enough multi-camera visibility** (many bodyparts only have 1 camera observation in those frames).

And `swap=UNKNOWN` is a downstream consequence: if `head`/`tail_root` rarely triangulate, Stage B can’t bootstrap swap/no-swap continuity.

Below is the most efficient way to continue.

---

## 1) First determine if the data *allows* triangulation
Before tuning more parameters, check how often each bodypart has ≥2 cameras with *any* detection (either mouse). If that number is low, `3D=0` is expected and no gate tuning will fix it.

Run this **in the shell** (not inside the Python REPL):

```bash
python - <<'PY'
import pandas as pd

df = pd.read_csv("../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_long.csv")

# keep only finite points (DLC can have NaN)
df = df[df["x"].notna() & df["y"].notna()]

# for each (frame, bodypart, camera): does at least one individual exist?
cam_present = (df.groupby(["frame","bodypart","camera"])
                 .size()
                 .reset_index(name="n")
                 .assign(present=1))

# camera count per (frame, bodypart)
cam_count = cam_present.groupby(["frame","bodypart"])["present"].sum().reset_index(name="cams")

# summarize
print("cams per (frame,bodypart):")
print(cam_count["cams"].value_counts().sort_index())

print("\n% of (frame,bodypart) with >=2 cams:", (cam_count["cams"]>=2).mean())
print("% with 3 cams:", (cam_count["cams"]==3).mean())

# per-bodypart breakdown
print("\nPer bodypart, % with >=2 cams:")
print(cam_count.assign(ok=cam_count["cams"]>=2).groupby("bodypart")["ok"].mean().sort_values(ascending=False))
PY
```

If you see that “≥2 cams” is, say, only 5–10% for many parts, then the low 3D yield is fundamentally “visibility limited”.

---

## 2) If multi-camera coverage is decent: relax the bbox gate
Your `StageAParams` **does have** `bbox_margin_mm` (default 20), but your `run_mouse3d.py` doesn’t expose it yet. You can set it directly.

In `run_mouse3d.py`, after you set `params.stage_a.d_max_mm` etc., add:

```python
params.stage_a.bbox_margin_mm = 1000.0   # diagnostic: effectively disables bbox gate
```

Then rerun just a small range:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py \
  --cameras ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2/cameras.json \
  --dlc ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_long.csv \
  --seg-dir ../../mouse_seg/preds/out2m_2 \
  --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/tune_bbox \
  --frames 0 50 \
  --d-max 80 --e-init 50 --theta-trip 0.6 --theta-pair 0.4 \
  --debug
```

If `3D=` jumps noticeably, bbox gating was the culprit. Then we tighten it back to something sane (e.g. 150–300 mm margin) once we’re sure geometry is correct.

---

## 3) Turn on *file* debugging (JSONL) so you can inspect which parts fail
Your `pipeline.py` already supports:
- `debug=True` → per-frame printout
- `debug_save_path=...` → per-frame JSONL with per-bodypart items and stats fileciteturn7file6L113-L189

So, in `run_mouse3d.py`, add a CLI argument and pass it through:

```python
p.add_argument("--debug-save", default=None, help="Write per-frame debug JSONL")

# ...

recon = Mouse3DReconstructor(
    rig=rig, dlc=dlc, seg_source=seg_source, params=params,
    debug=args.debug,
    debug_save_path=args.debug_save,
)
```

This ties directly into the already-present debug logging in `Mouse3DReconstructor._debug_frame(...)`. fileciteturn7file6L113-L189

Then run:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... \
  --frames 0 500 \
  --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run_dbg \
  --debug \
  --debug-save ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run_dbg.jsonl
```

### Quick: how often do anchors triangulate?
```bash
python - <<'PY'
import json
from collections import Counter

path = "../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/run_dbg.jsonl"
cnt = Counter()
n = 0
with open(path) as f:
    for line in f:
        n += 1
        rec = json.loads(line)
        for bp in ("head","tail_root"):
            if any(it.get("P") is not None for it in rec["bodyparts"].get(bp, [])):
                cnt[bp] += 1
print("frames:", n, "anchor_3D_frames:", dict(cnt))
PY
```

If head/tail_root rarely triangulate, `swap` will stay UNKNOWN — that’s expected.

Assistant: Your coverage numbers basically eliminate “not enough cameras” as the cause:

- **≥2 cams available for ~98% of (frame, bodypart)** and **3 cams for ~78%**.
- For `head` and `tail_root`, **it’s 100% ≥2 cams**.

So when your console debug prints `3D=0` for many frames, it means **Stage A is rejecting hypotheses**, not that the data is missing. (In your debug print, `3D` counts items where `it.P is not None` fileciteturn8file6.)

Also, relaxing `d-max / e-init / theta-*` didn’t change anything → those gates are not the bottleneck.

### The most likely bottleneck now
In practice this almost always ends up being one of these:

1) **BBox gate** (too strict or wrong margin)  
2) **An epipolar gate** (if enabled with a too-small threshold or a wrong F)  
3) A bug/over-strictness in the “fast reprojection” gate (but you raised it and nothing changed)

You also noted your `run_mouse3d.py` doesn’t expose `bbox_margin_mm` fileciteturn8file2, so it’s likely stuck at a strict default inside Stage A.

from mice3d.stage_a import StageAParams

## 2) Quick diagnostic: effectively disable the bbox gate
Once you know the field name, do **one** of these (pick what matches your printed fields):

### If you have a margin field
Set it huge (temporarily):

```python
params.stage_a.bbox_margin_mm = 1000.0
```

(or whatever the name is in your printout)

### If you have an enable/disable flag
Disable it:

```python
params.stage_a.use_bbox_gate = False
```

Then rerun only 0–50 with `--debug`:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... --frames 0 50 --debug
```

**Expected outcome:** `3D=` should jump a lot (often 10–20+ per frame). If it does, you’ve found the culprit. Then we tighten bbox back to something reasonable (e.g. 200–300 mm margin) instead of disabling it permanently.

## 3) Add “Stage A gate failure histogram” so you don’t fly blind
Right now your debug JSONL (if you enable it) records final chosen items and stats, but it doesn’t say *which gate killed* the other hypotheses. Your `pipeline.py` is already designed to write per-frame JSON lines when `debug_save_path` is set. fileciteturn7file6L113-L189

**Small but powerful patch**: in `stage_a.py`, add counters like:

- `triplets_total`
- `triplets_fail_angle`, `fail_closest`, `fail_bbox`, `fail_fastreproj`, `fail_ba`
- same for pairs

and return them along with the items, or attach them to the `TriangulatedItem` list (e.g. as a `stagea_debug` dict). Then in `pipeline._debug_frame`, add it to the JSON line.

This lets you answer “why 0?” in 10 seconds.

If you want, paste the `StageAParams fields:` printout and I’ll tell you exactly where to patch in your current Stage A implementation.

---

## 4) Why `swap=UNKNOWN` forever (and how it fixes itself)
Swap state becomes meaningful only once you have **consistent 3D anchors** across frames. Since head/tail_root *should* be available multi-view almost always, the fact swap stays UNKNOWN is a symptom of the same Stage A rejection: anchor 3D points aren’t being produced frequently enough to bootstrap continuity.

Once Stage A yields more 3D, swap should start leaving UNKNOWN.

---

## 5) How to continue with “more frames” without drowning
Two practical patterns:

### A) “Tune first, then full run”
1) Tune on 0–200 with debug:
2) If good, run full 0–1800 without debug printing every frame.

```bash
# tune
python run_mouse3d.py ... --frames 0 200 --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/tune --debug

# full run
python run_mouse3d.py ... --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/full
```

### B) Redirect debug output to a file
```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... --frames 0 1000 --debug > ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/debug_stdout.txt
```

## Why bbox is the likely bottleneck
- Your coverage shows the points are there (≥2 cams almost always).
- Relaxing `d-max`, `e-init`, `theta-*` didn’t change 3D yield.
- So the remaining hard gate that can wipe out almost everything is bbox with a too-small margin, especially if:
  - your triangulated midpoint init sometimes lands a bit outside the physical cage, or
  - your cage origin/axes differ slightly from the camera rig convention.

---

Once bbox is relaxed and you see `3D=` increase, `swap` should stop being UNKNOWN frequently, because anchors (`head`, `tail_root`) will start producing stable 3D tracks.

Also, since your `run_mouse3d.py` already supports `--debug-save`, you can log per-frame details right away: fileciteturn9file0L89-L99

```bash

  --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/tune_bbox
```

It will write `.../tune_bbox_debug.jsonl` automatically. fileciteturn9file0L158-L186

Assistant: Got it. Since:

- your DLC coverage is excellent (≥2 cams for ~98% of (frame,bodypart), and **100%** for `head` and `tail_root`), and  
- changing `d-max / e-init / theta-*` and even effectively disabling bbox **does not change the 3D yield**,

we need to stop guessing which gate is blocking and **measure what’s happening**.

There are **two high-probability explanations**:

1) **Stage A is not even attempting BA** for most hypotheses (a pre-gate blocks everything), or  
2) BA is attempted but **nothing ever meets the acceptance condition** (or Stage B discards triangulations — less likely, but we should verify).

Below is the fastest path to pin it down.

---

## 1) Verify your overridden Stage A params are actually the ones being used

In your current `run_mouse3d.py`, the Stage A params you set from CLI are here (accept_rms/e_init/d_max/theta). fileciteturn12file2  
Add this right after you finish setting `params.stage_a.*` (same block):

```python
print("StageAParams (effective):", params.stage_a.__dict__)
```

Then run just one frame:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... --frames 0 1 --debug
```

This eliminates “edited wrong file / wrong place / value overwritten later”.

---

## 2) Check whether Stage B is discarding 3D points (quick sanity check)
Right now the console `3D=` number is computed from **Stage B results** only. fileciteturn12file0  
Patch `mice3d/pipeline.py` so it prints **both Stage A and Stage B 3D counts**:

In `_debug_frame`, replace the existing debug block with:

```python
if self.debug:
    def count_3d(stage):
        n3d = 0
        for _, items in stage.items():
            for it in items:
                if it.P is not None:
                    n3d += 1
        return n3d

    n3dA = count_3d(stageA)
    n3dB = count_3d(stageB)

    # old stats (mean RMS) stays based on stageB, fine
    nitems = sum(len(items) for items in stageB.values())
    rms_vals = [
        float(it.stats.rms_px)
        for items in stageB.values()
        for it in items
        if it.P is not None and it.stats is not None and np.isfinite(it.stats.rms_px)
    ]
    rms_mean = float(np.mean(rms_vals)) if rms_vals else float("nan")
    print(f"[frame {frame}] items={nitems} 3D_A={n3dA} 3D_B={n3dB} mean_rms_px={rms_mean:.3f} swap={self.prev_state.swap_state}")
```

If you see `3D_A > 0` but `3D_B == 0`, then Stage B is dropping triangulations and we fix Stage B.  
If both are zero, the problem is purely Stage A.

---

## 3) Use `--trace-ceres` on a “3D=0” frame to see whether BA is even being called
In your runner, `--trace-ceres` turns on printing for each Ceres solve call. fileciteturn12file2

Run a single frame that currently shows `3D=0`, e.g. frame 0:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... --frames 0 1 --trace-ceres --verbose-ceres
```

Interpretation:

- **No `[TRACE ceres_point_ba]` lines at all**  
  → all hypotheses are rejected *before* BA (a pre-gate or a logic bug).

- **Many trace lines, but still `3D=0`**  
  → BA is run, but the post-check rejects all (RMS threshold / stats / acceptance logic).

This single test is extremely informative.

---

## 4) A diagnostic script that bypasses Stage A gates completely (ground truth check)
This answers the key question: **Is there a consistent triplet/pair in the data for a given frame+bodypart?**

Save as `python/diagnose_frame.py`:

```python
import json
import itertools
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd

import ceres_point_ba  # your compiled module

def load_rig(cameras_json):
    with open(cameras_json, "r") as f:
        j = json.load(f)
    cams = j["cameras"]
    cams_sorted = sorted(cams, key=lambda c: c["name"])
    C = len(cams_sorted)
    fx = np.array([c["fx"] for c in cams_sorted], float)
    fy = np.array([c["fy"] for c in cams_sorted], float)
    cx = np.array([c["cx"] for c in cams_sorted], float)
    cy = np.array([c["cy"] for c in cams_sorted], float)
    R = np.array([c["R"] for c in cams_sorted], float)     # world->cam
    t = np.array([c["t"] for c in cams_sorted], float)     # world->cam
    names = [c["name"] for c in cams_sorted]
    return {"fx":fx,"fy":fy,"cx":cx,"cy":cy,"R":R,"t":t,"names":names}

def cam_center_world(R, t):
    # Pc = R Pw + t  =>  C = -R^T t
    return -R.T @ t

def ray_world_from_uv(rig, cam_idx, uv):
    fx,fy,cx,cy = rig["fx"][cam_idx], rig["fy"][cam_idx], rig["cx"][cam_idx], rig["cy"][cam_idx]
    R = rig["R"][cam_idx]
    t = rig["t"][cam_idx]
    x = (uv[0]-cx)/fx
    y = (uv[1]-cy)/fy
    d_c = np.array([x,y,1.0], float)
    d_c /= np.linalg.norm(d_c)
    d_w = R.T @ d_c
    d_w /= np.linalg.norm(d_w)
    C = cam_center_world(R, t)
    return C, d_w

def closest_midpoint_two_rays(C1,d1,C2,d2):
    # returns midpoint between closest points on two skew lines
    w0 = C1 - C2
    a = np.dot(d1,d1)
    b = np.dot(d1,d2)
    c = np.dot(d2,d2)
    d = np.dot(d1,w0)
    e = np.dot(d2,w0)
    denom = a*c - b*b
    if abs(denom) < 1e-12:
        # nearly parallel: pick arbitrary
        s = 0.0
        t = e/c if c>1e-12 else 0.0
    else:
        s = (b*e - c*d)/denom
        t = (a*e - b*d)/denom
    P1 = C1 + s*d1
    P2 = C2 + t*d2
    return 0.5*(P1+P2), np.linalg.norm(P1-P2)

def angle_deg(d1,d2):
    c = np.clip(np.dot(d1,d2)/(np.linalg.norm(d1)*np.linalg.norm(d2)), -1.0, 1.0)
    return float(np.degrees(np.arccos(c)))

def solve_point(P_init, cam_idx, uv, rig, sigma_pix=2.0):
    cams = {"fx": rig["fx"], "fy": rig["fy"], "cx": rig["cx"], "cy": rig["cy"], "R": rig["R"], "t": rig["t"]}
    P_ref, stats = ceres_point_ba.solve_point(
        np.asarray(P_init, float),
        list(map(int, cam_idx)),
        np.asarray(uv, float),
        cams,
        sigmas=None,
        sigma_pix=float(sigma_pix),
        max_num_iterations=50,
        loss="huber",
        loss_scale=1.0,
        verbose=False,
    )
    return np.asarray(P_ref, float), stats

def main():
    import argparse
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    ap.add_argument("--cameras", required=True)
    ap.add_argument("--dlc", required=True)
    ap.add_argument("--frame", type=int, required=True)
    ap.add_argument("--bodypart", required=True)
    ap.add_argument("--sigma", type=float, default=2.0)
    ap.add_argument("--max-rms", type=float, default=6.0)
    args = ap.parse_args()

    rig = load_rig(args.cameras)
    df = pd.read_csv(args.dlc)
    df = df[(df["frame"]==args.frame) & (df["bodypart"]==args.bodypart)]
    df = df[df["x"].notna() & df["y"].notna()]

    # build candidates per camera: list of (dlc_id, uv)
    cam_to_cands = {name: [] for name in rig["names"]}
    for _,r in df.iterrows():
        cam = r["camera"]
        if cam in cam_to_cands:
            cam_to_cands[cam].append((int(r["individual"].replace("mouse","")) if isinstance(r["individual"], str) else int(r["individual"]),
                                      np.array([r["x"], r["y"]], float)))

    # map names->idx
    name_to_idx = {n:i for i,n in enumerate(rig["names"])}

    cams_present = [c for c,v in cam_to_cands.items() if len(v)>0]
    print("cams_present:", cams_present, "counts:", {c:len(cam_to_cands[c]) for c in cams_present})
    if len(cams_present) < 2:
        print("Not enough cameras.")
        return

    # enumerate triplets if 3 cams present, else pairs only
    best = []
    cam_trip = [c for c in rig["names"] if len(cam_to_cands[c])>0]
    # limit to first 3 cameras if more (should be exactly 3)
    cam_trip = cam_trip[:3]

    def test_combo(cam_names, choice):
        cam_idx = []
        uv = []
        rays = []
        for cam_name,(dlc_id,uv_i) in zip(cam_names, choice):
            ci = name_to_idx[cam_name]
            cam_idx.append(ci)
            uv.append(uv_i)
            C,d = ray_world_from_uv(rig, ci, uv_i)
            rays.append((C,d))
        # init from best pair among those rays
        best_init = None
        best_gap = 1e18
        for (C1,d1),(C2,d2) in itertools.combinations(rays,2):
            P0,gap = closest_midpoint_two_rays(C1,d1,C2,d2)
            if gap < best_gap:
                best_gap = gap
                best_init = P0
        P_ref, stats = solve_point(best_init, cam_idx, uv, rig, sigma_pix=args.sigma)
        return {
            "cams": cam_names,
            "dlc_ids": [x[0] for x in choice],
            "rms": float(stats["rms_px"]),
            "max": float(stats["max_err_px"]),
            "gap_init_mm": float(best_gap),
            "P": P_ref,
        }

    # triplets
    if len(cam_trip) == 3:
        combos = list(itertools.product(*[cam_to_cands[c] for c in cam_trip]))
        print("Triplet combos:", len(combos))
        for choice in combos:
            res = test_combo(cam_trip, choice)
            best.append(res)

    # pairs
    for camA, camB in itertools.combinations([c for c in rig["names"] if len(cam_to_cands[c])>0], 2):
        combos = list(itertools.product(cam_to_cands[camA], cam_to_cands[camB]))
        print(f"Pair combos {camA}-{camB}:", len(combos))
        for choice in combos:
            res = test_combo([camA, camB], choice)
            best.append(res)

    best.sort(key=lambda r: r["rms"])
    print("\nTop 10 by RMS:")
    for r in best[:10]:
        ok = "OK" if r["rms"] <= args.max_rms else "bad"
        print(ok, "cams", r["cams"], "dlc_ids", r["dlc_ids"], "rms", r["rms"], "max", r["max"], "gap_init_mm", r["gap_init_mm"])

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

Run it on a frame where Stage A gives you `3D=0` (e.g. frame 0) and a stable part:

```bash
python diagnose_frame.py \
  --cameras ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2/cameras.json \
  --dlc ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_long.csv \
  --frame 0 \
  --bodypart head
```

Interpretation:

- If the script prints several `OK ... rms < 6`, then **the data is geometrically consistent** and Stage A is blocking incorrectly → we instrument Stage A to find which gate (or fix a units bug, e.g. degrees vs radians).
- If *all* triplets/pairs have huge RMS, then for that frame+part your DLC outputs are inconsistent across cameras even after trying all combinations — which explains `3D=0`.

This diagnostic bypasses all Stage A gates, so it’s a ground-truth check.

## 5) Why `swap=UNKNOWN` still makes sense right now
Swap estimation needs anchor 3D continuity. Your current triangulation yield is ~0–3 3D points per frame, so it’s normal that `swap` never stabilizes.

Once Stage A yields `head` and `tail_root` 3D in most frames, swap will leave UNKNOWN.

Assistant: You’ve basically reached the point where **parameter-tweaking in Stage A won’t change anything** until you confirm two things:

1) **Which code you’re actually running** (local file vs an installed `mice3d` in site-packages), and  
2) Whether **Stage B is actually seeing segmentation masks for the frames you think it is**.

Those two explain *both* “`bbox_margin_mm` doesn’t exist in `run_mouse3d.py`” and “I changed it but nothing changes”, and also why you see so many frames with `3D=0`.

---

## 1) First: verify you’re editing the code that’s actually being imported

Run this **from the same shell/env** you run `run_mouse3d.py` with:

```bash
python - <<'PY'
import mice3d, mice3d.stage_a, mice3d.segmentation
print("mice3d:", mice3d.__file__)
print("stage_a:", mice3d.stage_a.__file__)
print("segmentation:", mice3d.segmentation.__file__)
from mice3d.stage_a import StageAParams
print("StageAParams().bbox_margin_mm =", StageAParams().bbox_margin_mm)
PY
```

If those paths point into something like `.../site-packages/...`, then you can edit your local files all day and **nothing will change**. In that case run with your repo on the path, e.g.:

```bash
PYTHONPATH="$(pwd)" python run_mouse3d.py ...
```

(or install editable once: `pip install -e ..` from the repo root, if you have packaging set up).

**This is the #1 reason** “I changed `bbox_margin_mm` but nothing changes.”

---

## 2) Why `bbox_margin_mm` isn’t in `run_mouse3d.py`

`bbox_margin_mm` is a **field of `StageAParams`** (as your printout shows), but your `run_mouse3d.py` simply **doesn’t expose it as a CLI argument**.

So the right mental model is:

- `StageAParams` has `bbox_margin_mm`
- Your `run_mouse3d.py` may or may not set it
- If it doesn’t, changing CLI args won’t affect it

To make it tunable, add an argparse flag and assign it when building params, e.g.:

```python
# argparse
parser.add_argument("--bbox-margin-mm", type=float, default=20.0)

# when building the pipeline params
params.stage_a.bbox_margin_mm = args.bbox_margin_mm
```

And in `--debug`, print effective params once:

```python
if args.debug:
    print("StageA bbox_margin_mm:", params.stage_a.bbox_margin_mm)
```

That immediately tells you whether your edits are actually live.

---

## 3) Your `3D=0` pattern is *very likely segmentation lookup mismatch*, not Stage A thresholds

In your pipeline, it’s common to count “3D” as **assigned 3D** (i.e., Stage B gave it a mouse id). If Stage B can’t load masks for that frame/cam, you can easily get:

- lots of DLC observations (`items=52`),
- Stage A even triangulates internally,
- but Stage B can’t assign → you record **0 assigned 3D**.

Given your masks are named `mask_000001.png` etc and your frames start at 0, **frame↔mask off-by-one** is the classic culprit.

### Quick check: does Stage B actually see segmentation weights?
Look inside your assignments CSV:

```bash
python - <<'PY'
import pandas as pd
a = pd.read_csv("../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/tuneA_dlc_assignments.csv")
print("rows:", len(a))
print("seg_w_m0 is null fraction:", a["seg_w_m0"].isna().mean())
print("seg_w_m1 is null fraction:", a["seg_w_m1"].isna().mean())
print("new_mouse_id is null fraction:", a["new_mouse_id"].isna().mean())
PY
```

Interpretation:
- If `seg_w_*` is **almost always NaN/empty**, Stage B isn’t loading masks (wrong dirs/pattern/offset).
- If `seg_w_*` exists but `new_mouse_id` is often null, assignment logic is failing (separate issue).

---

## 4) Fix for `diagnose_frame.py`: `ceres_point_ba` import

That error is purely Python path. You ran `diagnose_frame.py` from the `python/` directory, but your compiled `ceres_point_ba*.so` is very likely **one directory up**.

### Fastest fix (no code changes)
```bash
PYTHONPATH="..:$PYTHONPATH" python diagnose_frame.py \
  --cameras ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2/cameras.json \
  --dlc ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_long.csv \
  --frame 0 \
  --bodypart head
```

### Permanent fix (add to `diagnose_frame.py`)
At the top:

```python
from pathlib import Path
import sys
sys.path.insert(0, str(Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]))  # adds repo root
import ceres_point_ba
```

(If the `.so` lives somewhere else, point to that folder.)

---

## 5) How to proceed with “more frames” in a way that actually debugs

### A. Run in blocks + summarize yield
Run, say, 0–2000:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py \
  --cameras ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2/cameras.json \
  --dlc ../../mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_long.csv \
  --seg-dir ../../mouse_seg/preds/out2m_2 \
  --out ../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/block0_2000 \
  --frames 0 2000 \
  --debug
```

Then summarize how many assigned 3D you actually got:

```bash
python - <<'PY'
import pandas as pd
t = pd.read_csv("../dlc_cleaned/out2m_2/block0_2000_triangulated3d.csv")
print("rows:", len(t))
print("frames with any 3D:", t["frame"].nunique())
per = t.groupby("frame").size()
print(per.describe())
PY
```

If that looks wrong (too sparse), **don’t tune Stage A yet** — go back to segmentation lookup.

### B. Pick one “bad” frame and one “good” frame
From your debug log, choose:
- one frame with `3D=0`
- one frame with `3D>0`

Run `diagnose_frame.py` on both **after fixing `ceres_point_ba` import**. That tells you if Stage A is producing good hypotheses but Stage B drops them, or if Stage A is failing.

### C. Only then tune thresholds
If (and only if) diagnose shows Stage A rejecting good triangulations, tune:
- `--accept-rms-triplet` / `--accept-rms-pair` (if you have them)
- `--likelihood-min` (lower it if DLC is sparse)
- `--d-max`, `--e-init` (usually *not* the limiting factor if your BA RMS is ~0.4 px)

But your trace output already shows many BA runs converging to low cost → Stage A is probably fine.

---

## 6) Segmentation naming flexibility (front/side/top + mask_000001)
If you want the code to be “smart” instead of renaming files, the robust approach is:

- **Map camera name → subdir** by fuzzy token match (`cam1_top` → `top`)
- **Detect frame offset** from the smallest index on disk (e.g. files start at 1 → offset = +1)
- **Detect filename pattern** by regex and build an index

If you paste your actual camera names from `cameras.json` (the `"name"` fields) and one `ls` of each seg folder (first ~5 filenames), I can give you a drop-in `SegmentationDirectorySource` that does exactly that.

(But you can already confirm the off-by-one hypothesis quickly: check whether `.../top/mask_000000.png` exists; if not, your frame0 will never get a mask unless you offset.)

---

If you do just two things next, do these:

1) Run the `__file__` snippet to confirm you’re editing the right code.  
2) Run the assignments CSV check (`seg_w_m0` null fraction) to confirm whether masks are actually being read.

Post those two outputs and I’ll tell you exactly which branch you’re on (path problem vs segmentation lookup vs assignment logic) and what to change.

## Add the CLI flag in `run_mouse3d.py`
You only need to wire one boolean into params:

1) Add the argparse flag:
```python
parser.add_argument(
    "--debug_stageA",
    action="store_true",
    help="Print detailed StageA hypothesis tests (inputs, all gates, BA convergence, end reasons).",
)
```

2) After you build your params object:
```python
params.stage_a.debug_stageA = args.debug_stageA
```

That’s it.

### (Optional but recommended) expose bbox margin on CLI too
Since you were experimenting with bbox margins:
```python
parser.add_argument("--bbox-margin-mm", type=float, default=None)

# ...
if args.bbox_margin_mm is not None:
    params.stage_a.bbox_margin_mm = args.bbox_margin_mm
```

---

## Why your “bbox margin = 1000” didn’t change anything
Even with a huge bbox margin, **nothing will change if hypotheses are being rejected earlier** (theta / d_closest / e_init / BA success / RMS threshold). Your per-frame logs showing lots of `3D=0` is consistent with “all hypotheses get rejected somewhere”—and bbox might not be the limiting gate at all.

With `--debug_stageA`, you’ll immediately see which gate is killing them (and with what numeric margin).

---

## Quick note about your `diagnose_frame.py` crash
You already fixed the import via `PYTHONPATH=..`. The remaining error:
`ValueError: too many values to unpack (expected 2)`
is because `ceres_point_ba.solve_point(...)` returns a **single dict**, not `(P_ref, stats)`. So you want:
```python
out = ceres_point_ba.solve_point(...)
P_ref = out["P"]
stats = out
```
